1801 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Byers


Crim. No. 9206


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


90 Cal. App. 3d 140; 153 Cal. Rptr. 249; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1460



February 21, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied March 19, 1979, and the Petitions of Appellants Byers and Higgins for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied May 10, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Butte County, No. 61061, Lucian B. Vandegrift, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, real estate sellers, appealed judgments of the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which convicted them of violating Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 11010, 11018.1, 11022, and 11023, for failing to file a notice of intention to subdivide and sell land, offering parcels for sale without providing a public report, and engaging in false and misleading advertising concerning the sale.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that defendants, real estate sellers, violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 11010, 11018.1, 11022, and 11023, which were part of the Subdivided Lands Act, by failing to file a notice of intention to subdivide and sell parcels of land, offering parcels for sale without providing a public report, and engaging in false and misleading advertising concerning the land. The court rejected defendants' constitutional challenge to the law and held that regulation of subdivision of lands did not deprive them of any fundamental liberty, but was instead a limited economic regulation of real property for the public's protection. The court found that defendants' conviction was supported by the evidence because it established their participation in a series of unlawful transactions, which was sufficient to show that they aided and abetted illegal conduct. The court rejected defendants' arguments that the lower court subjected them to double jeopardy when it dismissed the deadlocked trial jury. The court held that the record showed that the jury was at a stalemate and that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that defendants, real estate sellers, violated several provisions of the Subdivided Lands Act. The court held that regulation of land subdivisions did not deprive defendants of any fundamental liberty, and that the evidence establishing defendants' participation in a series of unlawful transactions was sufficient to support their convictions.

 

1802 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Kerlin v. Board of Administration


Civ. No. 15837


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


90 Cal. App. 3d 317; 153 Cal. Rptr. 257; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1479



February 21, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 12, 1979. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 19, 1979. Bird, C. J., did not Participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 250954, Irving H. Perluss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, former wife, challenged a substantive decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) that held that the provisions of Cal. Gov't. Code § 21205, dealing with beneficiaries of a deceased state employee, were constitutional. Plaintiff also challenged the decision of the superior court to not hear any further matters.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, former wife, was married to a public employee who was a member of the Public Employees Retirement System (PERS). The employee designated plaintiff as his beneficiary under PERS. They divorced, then he re-married and later died without changing his beneficiary. Before he died, the legislature had passed Cal. Gov't. Code § 21205, which provided that dissolution of marriage constituted an automatic revocation of an employee's previous revocable designation of beneficiary under PERS. His wife at the time of his death received compensation under PERS because she was considered the statutory beneficiary. Plaintiff made a claim for benefits but the claim was denied. In affirming the decision of the superior court, the court held that § 21205 was not unconstitutional because the legislative changes were materially related to the theory of a pension system and its successful operation. The members of PERS received advantages as well as disadvantages. The court also affirmed the decision of the superior court not to hear any other matters than the constitutionality of § 21205.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's ruling that the challenged statute, dealing with beneficiaries of a deceased state employee, was constitutional. The court further held that the superior court did not err in refusing to hear matters other than the constitutional question.

 

1803 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Residents Ad Hoc Stadium Com. v. Board of Trustees


Civ. No. 17414


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


89 Cal. App. 3d 274; 152 Cal. Rptr. 585; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1378



February 7, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On February 20, 1979, the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Hearing Denied April 4, 1979. Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 9, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 204809-8, Frank J. Creede, Jr., Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a committee of residents, appealed from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which found that an environmental impact report adequately supported the decision of defendants, university and college trustees, to approve and authorize construction of an athletic stadium.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, university and college trustees, approved and authorized the construction of an athletic stadium located in the northwest area of the campus. Their decision was supported by an en environmental impact report (EIR). At the time of acquisition, the proposed site was surrounded largely by open agricultural land. When the EIR was prepared, the surrounding area was developed residentially with single family homes, apartments, sorority and fraternity houses, and the university campus. Plaintiffs, a committee of residents, filed suit seeking to invalidate the EIR as a post hoc rationalization of the project, to enjoin solicitation of building funds for the stadium, and to determine that the scope of judicial review as provided in Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 21168, was unconstitutional. From an adverse judgment, plaintiffs appealed, contending that §§ 21168 and 21168.5 violated equal protection, that the trustees' determination was invalid, the EIR was inadequate and invalid, and that they were entitled to attorney fees. After review, the court concluded that all of plaintiffs' contentions were without merit. Thus, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that found that an environmental impact report (EIR) supported the decision of defendants, university and college trustees, to approve and authorize construction of an athletic stadium was affirmed because there was no violation of equal protection, the trustees' determination was valid, and the EIR was adequate and not defective.

 

1804 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


PINION v. BOARD OF RETIREMENT OF THE FRESNO CTY. EMPLES. RETIREMENT ASSN.


Civ. No. 2810.


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


89 Cal. App. 3d 228; 152 Cal. Rptr. 383; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1373



Feb. 6, 1979.


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Hg. den. Apr. 9, 1979, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14  [**1] Rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 159671, Joseph L. Joy, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged an order of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which denied appellant's petition for a writ of administrative mandate seeking to set aside respondent retirement board's decision to deny appellant's application for disability retirement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer retired because he suffered from heart disease. Appellant applied for service-connected disability retirement, but respondent retirement board denied the request on the ground that appellant's heart condition did not arise out of his employment. The trial court upheld respondent's decision and denied appellant's writ of mandate. The court reversed and remanded to the trial court to issue a writ of administrative mandate ordering respondent to award appellant service-connected disability benefits on the basis of a heart disease arising out of and in the course of his employment. The court held that it was error for the board to base its decision on the testimony of one doctor because it did not rebut the presumption of Cal. Gov't Code § 31720.5 that in the absence of contrary evidence, heart trouble developed by an officer was a disease arising out of employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision denying appellant police officer's writ of mandate and remanded to the trial court to order respondent retirement board to award appellant disability benefits because there was a presumption that appellant's heart disease arose out of the course of his employment.

 

1805 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Hodges


Crim. No. 9895


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


89 Cal. App. 3d 221; 152 Cal. Rptr. 394; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1372



February 6, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 9, 1979.



DISPOSITION: The petition for habeas corpus is denied; the order to show cause is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought habeas corpus review to require that he be given credit for time served in state prison following his return there as an escaped prisoner, and while subsequent charges were pending.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought credit for time in state prison pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5, following his return there as an escaped prisoner. The sentence against which credit was sought was imposed for a charge which was brought after petitioner's apprehension, and that arose out of petitioner's conduct at the time of his arrest as an escapee. Petitioner argued that he was entitled to credit for the time he was in prison between being arraigned on the subsequent charges, and the time sentence was imposed. The court denied the writ of habeas corpus sought, finding that the purpose of § 2900.5 was to prevent inequality to impoverished defendants who could not make bail and were required to remain in custody during the proceedings. The court found that petitioner's status as a state prisoner was not due to the subsequent charges, but the prior prison commitment, and the credit provisions of § 2900.5 should not apply to petitioner's situation.


OUTCOME: Writ of habeas corpus was denied because petitioner was not entitled to credit for time served in state prison pending resolution of charges for offenses subsequent to his original sentence because his imprisonment was not due to poverty and inability to make bail during the proceedings, but rather his previous prison sentence.

 

1806 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Milano


Crim. No. 33206


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


89 Cal. App. 3d 153; 152 Cal. Rptr. 318; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1366



February 2, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 12, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 337000, Stanley R. Malone, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The conviction of appellant Brian Callahan is reversed. All other judgments of conviction herein are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) that convicted them of an attempt to violate Cal. Penal Code § 337i concerning dissemination of gambling information.


OVERVIEW: Four defendants were jointly charged with attempted dissemination of gambling information, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 664, 337i, and bookmaking, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § section 337a (§ 337a). As to each defendant, the charge of violation of § 337a was dismissed. Each defendant also moved to dismiss, on the ground that Cal. Penal Code § 337i (§ 337i) was unconstitutional. Each motion was denied. Defendants were then convicted, in three separate trials, of attempt to violate § 337i. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions of all but one defendant, finding that the evidence was insufficient to support that defendant's conviction. As to defendants' remaining contentions, the court held that § 337i was not constitutionally infirm and did not violate defendants' right to equal protection and that defendants were not subjected to discriminatory enforcement of the statute against them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction of one defendant, on grounds of insufficient evidence; the court affirmed the judgments of conviction for the remaining defendants, holding, inter alia, that the evidence was sufficient to support their convictions and that the statute under which they were convicted was not constitutionally infirm.

 

1807 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frost


Crim. No. 17646.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


88 Cal. App. 3d 838; 152 Cal. Rptr. 102; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1336



Jan. 26, 1979.


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Hg. den. Mar. 22, 1979, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art VI, § 14  [**1] Rule 976, Cal Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Monterey County, No. CR 5173, Harkjoon Paik, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for first-degree murder under the felony-murder rule and first-degree robbery that were entered in the Superior Court of Monterey County (California). Appellant argued that Cal. Penal Code § 1181 violated his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of first-degree murder under the felony-murder rule, and first-degree robbery. The trial judge modified the murder verdict to second-degree murder. The court reversed and ordered the first-degree murder verdict reinstated. The trial judge amended the judgment as directed; appellant now appeals from that action of the trial court. Cal. Penal Code § 1181(6) provided that when the verdict or finding was contrary to law or evidence, but if the evidence showed the defendant to be not guilty of the degree of the crime of which he was convicted, but guilty of a lesser degree thereof, or of a lesser crime included, the court could modify the verdict without granting or ordering a new trial. This power extended to any court to which the cause may be appealed. Appellant's conviction as originally modified by the trial judge was reinstated because the statutory scheme discriminated impermissibly between similarly situated persons in that it allowed the People to appeal an order reducing a conviction to a lesser degree of the same offense but did not allow an appeal of an order reducing a conviction to a lesser-included offense.


OUTCOME: Appellant's first-degree murder conviction was reversed and reinstated as originally modified by the trial court because the statutory scheme used by the People to appeal certain convictions deprived appellant of equal protection of the law.

 

1808 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Banks


Crim. No. 10103


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


88 Cal. App. 3d 864; 152 Cal. Rptr. 111; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1340



January 26, 1979 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus to contest his detention in a state mental hospital (California) for more than six months after he was found mentally incompetent to stand trial for brandishing a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with brandishing a deadly weapon. He pled not guilty by reason of insanity and he was thereafter found mentally incompetent to stand trial. Criminal proceedings were suspended and he was committed to a state hospital. Petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus after he had been confined for six months. The prosecution resisted. The due process clauses, federal and state, were the most basic substantive checks on government's power to act unfairly or oppressively. As such, they protected against infringements by the state upon those fundamental rights implicit in the concept of ordered liberty. Due process forbade the arbitrary deprivation of liberty and, in the context of commitment to a mental hospital required at least that the nature and duration of commitment bear some reasonable relation to the purpose for which the individual was committed. However, in the case of the incompetent defendant, the state might have a legitimate interest in obtaining a conviction, an interest not present in the case of either mentally disordered sex offenders or those found not guilty by reason of insanity. The petition was denied, as petitioner had been released.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied because petitioner had already been released from confinement in the state mental hospital. The case was literally moot.

Hiatt v. Berkeley


Civ. No. 39033.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


88 Cal. App. 3d 503; 151 Cal. Rptr. 895; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1310



Jan. 19, 1979 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Mar. 28, 1979 (S.F. 24005)
June 19, 1980, cause retrans. to Ct. of App., 1st Dist., Div. 2, for reconsideration in light of Price v. Civil Com., 26 Cal.3d 257 and United Steel Workers v. Weber (1979) 443 U.S. 193 (See 130 C.A.3d 298)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 453459-2, Lyle E. Cook, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which awarded damages to plaintiff employees of city fire department and enjoined defendant from enforcement of certain provisions of its affirmative action program, in connection with a suit alleging reverse racial discrimination. Defendants alleged that discrimination was aimed at addressing past injustices and prior unequal treatment.


OVERVIEW: Although, plaintiff employees of defendant city fire department ranked higher in an examination, a minority candidate was promoted. Plaintiffs brought an action against defendant challenging the promotional procedures in defendant's affirmative action program (AAP) and invoking U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and the California constitution, plaintiffs claimed that AAP set rigid quotas in hiring and promoting employees based on race or sex. The trial court issued awarded plaintiffs damages and a permanent injunction in defendant's favor. Defendant appealed, claiming that discrimination was aimed at addressing past injustices and prior unequal treatment. The court reversed the trial court's decision in so far as it failed to make an award of attorney's fees to plaintiffs. The court also reversed the trial court's judgment enjoining defendant's AAP pertaining to use of written tests and employment list qualifying categories, finding that defendant failed to prove that racial classifications in AAP were warranted by compelling government interest. The court, affirming all other aspects, stated that there was no record that employees at the fire department ever suffered discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision insofar as it failed to make an award of attorney's fees to plaintiff employees of defendant city's fire department. The court also reversed portions of the trial court's judgment enjoining defendant's affirmative action program pertaining to use of written tests and the employment list qualifying categories. The court, however, affirmed all other aspects of the trial court's judgment.

 

1810 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Synanon Foundation, Inc.


Civ. No. 3743


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


88 Cal. App. 3d 304; 151 Cal. Rptr. 757; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1293



January 15, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 9, 1979, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 14, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Tulare County, No. 85773, Leonard M. Ginsburg, Judge. *


* Retired judge of the superior court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant charitable foundation sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which granted respondent county's request to enjoin it from operating its airport because it was an alleged public nuisance per se. Appellant contended that there was no balancing of the equities, which precluded the granting of the injunction.


OVERVIEW: Respondent county sought to enjoin appellant charitable foundation's operation of an airport on its property. The complaint alleged that the airport was a public nuisance per se because it was being operated without a special use permit in violation of a zoning ordinance. The trial court entered a pretrial order enjoining appellant from operating the airport. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that it was not clear that the permit requirements of the ordinance applied to appellant's airport. Further, the court noted, that although the trial court stated in its decision granting the preliminary injunction that it had balanced the equities, it did not weigh the relative harm to the parties where it did not consider the possibility of interlocutory judicial error in its holding that the airport operation constituted a zoning violation. Even though there was a strong governmental interest in enforcing the zoning ordinance, appellant had made a strong showing of interim harm if the injunction should issue. Accordingly, the court held, the failure to balance this harm against the governmental interest in securing compliance with the ordinance was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The order enjoining appellant charitable foundation from operating its airport was reversed because the trial court's failure to balance interim harm caused by the injunction, against respondent county's interest in securing compliance with its ordinance, was an abuse of discretion.

 

1811 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barben


Crim. No. 33432


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


88 Cal. App. 3d 215; 151 Cal. Rptr. 717; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1284



January 11, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Long Beach Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. M 1132192, Eugene J. Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Municipal Court for the Long Beach Judicial District, Los Angeles County (California) of violating Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4050, which prohibited the sale of a poison, as defined in Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4160, by any person other than a registered pharmacist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was employed at an adult bookstore, sold a bottled room odorizer, and was prosecuted under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4050, which prohibited the sale of a poison by any person other than a registered pharmacist. He was convicted and sought review. The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that insofar as it relied on the definition of the term "poison" in Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4160, § 4050 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to attain the degree of certainty as to its application necessary to conform to constitutional due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, because the definition of the term "poison" on which it relied failed to sufficiently inform the public as to what was commanded or forbidden, and thus violated due process.

 

1812 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Longshore v. County of Ventura


Civ. No. 51425.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


88 Cal. App. 3d 126; 151 Cal. Rptr. 708; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1276



January 8, 1979 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Mar. 14, 1979 (L.A. 31090)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 59215, Steven J. Stone, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, retired deputy sheriff and active duty deputy sheriffs, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California) that sustained defendant county's demurrer and dismissed without leave to amend their suit for declaratory relief pursuant to a series of compensation ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Fiscal year 1960 to 1961 salary ordinances provided that authorized overtime could be compensated for only by compensatory time off. Fiscal year 1962 to 1963 salary ordinances provided for cash compensation for overtime if advance approval was obtained. Plaintiffs, retired deputy sheriff and active duty deputy sheriffs, worked for defendant county. Plaintiff retired deputy sheriff was promised compensation when he retired. Plaintiff retired deputy sheriff sought the monetary value of his accrued overtime and the remaining plaintiff sought a declaration that they were entitled to receive compensatory time off or the monetary equivalent thereof. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrers without leave to amend. Plaintiffs appealed. Defendant could be bound by equitable estoppel if plaintiffs were induced to refrain from taking compensatory time off or compensation. The court found no harmful effect on a public policy that would result from invoking estoppel. The court reversed because plaintiffs clearly sought a declaration of the effect of specified salary ordinances and there was no necessity that each plaintiff plead precisely the number of overtime hours accrued.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that dismissed plaintiffs' suit for declaratory relief under a series of compensation ordinances was reversed because defendant county could be equitably estopped to refrain from paying overtime compensation if plaintiffs were induced to refrain from taking compensatory time off or compensation because there would be no harmful effect on public policy.

 

1813 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Merandette v. City and County of San Francisco


Civ. No. 42511


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


88 Cal. App. 3d 105; 151 Cal. Rptr. 580; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1275



January 8, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 725316, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, lessors of blackjack machines, challenged a decision from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) denying them a preliminary injunction to prohibit respondents, city and county, from confiscating their video machines, and from arresting persons who manufactured, owned, or leased such machines. Appellants argued that Cal. Penal Code §§ 330a, 330b(1), 330b(2), and 330.1 were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, lessors of blackjack machines, challenged a decision denying a preliminary injunction to prohibit respondent, city and county, from confiscating video machines, and from arresting persons who manufactured, owned, or leased the machines. Respondent argued that the trial court could not properly enjoin the enforcement of pertinent statutes. Appellants argued that Cal. Penal Code §§ 330a, 330b(1), 330b(2), and 330.1 were unconstitutionally vague. Appellants contended their machines rewarded the winning player only with an additional chance to play the machine without cost. The court held that §§ 330b(1), 330b(2), and 330.1 explicitly stated that their prohibitions applied when the user of a machine, as a result of any element of hazard or chance, became entitled to receive anything of value or additional chance or right to use such machine or device, or to receive any token, whether of value or otherwise, entitling the holder to receive anything of value. Therefore, the statutes included within their prohibitions a machine that afforded the winner only the additional right to use that machine. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that the slot machine statutes were constitutional as applied to appellant lessors' device and their device, if found to be a game of chance, was prohibited by the terms of those statutes, because the reward of free games constituted a thing of value within the meaning of the statutes. The trial court therefore properly denied their request for a preliminary injunction.

 

1814 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Union Oil Co. v. Moesch


Civ. No. 53625


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


88 Cal. App. 3d 72; 151 Cal. Rptr. 517; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1271



January 5, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 197125, George M. Dell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lessee appealed a decision from the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) in favor of plaintiff lessor in an unlawful detainer action between a petroleum distributor landlord and retail gasoline franchisee. Plaintiff filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings, which the court granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lessee appealed a decision in an unlawful detainer action between a petroleum distributor and a retail gasoline franchisee. Plaintiff lessor filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings, which the court granted. Plaintiff argued that the factual issue of good cause to terminate the lease was immaterial because Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 20999.1, which prohibited termination without good cause, was enacted subsequent to the leasehold and thus could not be constitutionally applied. Defendant argued that no impairment of contract occurred because the lease terminated automatically and was thereafter renewed on a month-to-month basis subsequent to the statute's effective date. On appeal, the court reversed. Although generally a statute could not be applied retroactively to impair an existing contractual obligation, U.S. Const., art. I, § 10; Cal. Const., art. I, § 9, a month-to-month holdover was a new arrangement, not a continuation of the original lease. When the parties agreed upon the new arrangement, all law then applicable, including Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 20999, 20999.1, became a part of agreement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded in an appeal by defendant lessee from judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff lessor in an unlawful detainer action. The court held that a statute prohibiting termination of the lease between a petroleum distributor and a retail gasoline franchisee without good cause was applicable. The pleadings disclosed the possibility of an affirmative defense; it was error to grant judgment on the pleadings.

 

1815 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Rivera v. Los Angeles County Civil Service Com.


Civ. No. 53932


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


87 Cal. App. 3d 1001; 151 Cal. Rptr. 480; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1264



January 2, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 28, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 216830, Charles H. Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the preliminary injunction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged denial of her motion for preliminary injunction by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that would have prohibited respondent Los Angeles County Civil Service Commission from admitting her County Department of Public Social Services (DPSS) records as a client at her hearing in her suit challenging her employment termination from DPSS.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was a recipient of Aid to Families with Dependant Children (AFDC) under a program provided by her employer, the Department of Public Social Services. Appellant was dismissed from her employment based upon an allegation that she had accepted overpayments as a recipient of funds from the DPSS under the AFDC program. The court denied appellant's motion for a preliminary injunction prohibiting respondent Los Angeles County Civil Service Commission from admitting her records as a client from DPSS at her hearing challenging her dismissal from employment. Appellant sought review and contended that her records as a client of DPSS were confidential under Cal. Welf. & Instit. Code § 10850. On appeal, the lower court judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that appellant's situation fell within an exception to the protections accorded by § 10850 as her circumstances directly connected with the administration of the AFDC program. The court also found that application of the exception in § 10850 to appellant as eligibility worker-recipient did not violate her right of equal protection under either the United States or California Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment, which denied appellant employee's request to prohibit admission of her records as a client of AFDC program offered by her employer, County Department of Public Social Services, from the hearing challenging appellant's dismissal from employment, was affirmed. Appellant's records were not subject to statutory confidentiality protections because her employment was directly connected with administration of the AFDC program.

 

1816 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thomas


Crim. No. 32293


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


87 Cal. App. 3d 1014; 151 Cal. Rptr. 483; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 1266



January 2, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 29, 1979. Bird, C. J., and Manuel, J., did not Participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. A192337 and 32293, Bernard Lawler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of second-degree murder with a firearm by a jury in the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California). Appellant contended that inconsistencies in the prosecution witnesses' testimony rendered the evidence of guilt insufficient as a matter of law, that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury as to circumstantial evidence, and that the sentencing guidelines were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his second-degree murder conviction based on his claim that inconsistencies in the prosecution witnesses' testimony rendered the evidence of guilt insufficient as a matter of law, that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury as to circumstantial evidence, and that the sentencing guidelines were unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction, and held that the inconsistencies in witnesses' testimony were not severe and were mostly the result of differences in the chronology of events and the relative position of the participants, and because the incident occurred rather suddenly at a fairly well attended party. The court affirmed the lack of circumstantial evidence instruction because the direct evidence was not so fraught with inconsistencies that it could not have been considered direct evidence. As to sentencing, the court affirmed and held that appellant was not entitled to notice of the grounds upon which the court intended to rely in ordering the upper term of incarceration because appellant had been supplied with the probation officer's report, and any other reports and statements in aggravation or mitigation upon which the court relied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the witness testimony was not fraught with inconsistencies that would warrant a jury instruction as to circumstantial evidence and because the information upon which the court relied in sentencing appellant was available to appellant.

Capiscean Corp. v. Alcoholic Bev. Etc. Appeals Bd.

Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two

January 2, 1979 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] That portion of the Board's order affirming the decision of the Department with respect to alleged violations of the wine price maintenance schedule (count two) is annulled. The Board is directed to enter its order reversing the decision of the Department with respect to count two.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment from the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board (board) (California), in an action to suspend petitioner's license, where the board had affirmed the decision of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to suspend his license for sale of wine below the posted price, in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24755, and Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, § 99(a).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, holder of an off-sale general alcoholic beverage license issued by the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control (department), sold liquor and wine for less than the posted price to a department employee. After notice and hearing, the department found that petitioner had violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24755, and Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, § 99(a), in the sale of distilled spirits, and Cal. The court annulled with respect to alleged violations of the wine price maintenance schedule. The court had compared the statutes and regulations relating to price maintenance of distilled spirits and wine and found no difference.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the judgment from the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board (board) in an action to suspend petitioner's license, because the court had found no difference between the statutes and regulations relating to price maintenance of distilled spirits and wine.

De Lancie v. Superior Court of San Mateo County


Civ. No. 44283.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


97 Cal. App. 3d 519; 159 Cal. Rptr. 20; 1979 Cal. App. LEXIS 2197



Oct. 5, 1979 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Mod. of opn. on den. rehg. Nov. 1, 1979; Hg. granted Nov. 29, 1979 (S.F. 24095)
Mar. 25, 1981, case will be reheard when the court has its full complement of seven members. (See 31 C.3d 865)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, detainee and visitors, sought review of a decision of respondent, the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which sustained a demurrer without leave to amend, that related to the rights of pretrial detainees and their visitors to be free from indiscriminate covert electronic surveillance by jail officials, here real parties in interest.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, detainee and visitors, filed individual and class action complaints against jail officials, real parties in interest, challenging the legality of a covert electronic surveillance system that monitored conversations between detainees and their visitors. Petitioners challenged the decision of respondent court, which upheld the real parties' demurrer, and alleged the electronic surveillance system was in derogation of their rights under both the federal and state constitutions. The court overruled the trial court's granting of the demurrer, and held that the conduct was constitutionally impermissible under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1, because there was not a compelling governmental interest that justified the systematic surveillance operation. The court ruled that there was no compelling need to engage in such wholesale, indiscriminate intrusion into the area of a detainees' private conversation, particularly in the visiting room, therefore the conduct could not survive judicial scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the general demurrer in favor of jail officials, here real parties in interest, and held that petitioners, detainee and visitors, had validly stated a claim based upon the state constitution's right of privacy, because there was no compelling need to engage in indiscriminate intrusion into detainees' private conversations.

 

1820 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Hodges


Crim. No. 9895.


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


87 Cal. App. 3d 977; 151 Cal. Rptr. 475; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2250



Dec. 29, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehg. granted Jan. 24, 1979 (See 89 C.A.3d 221)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a request for a writ of habeas corpus demanding credit for time served in state prison, following his return there as an escaped prisoner, against a sentence imposed for charges brought after petitioner's apprehension that arose out of conduct related to his escape. Petitioner asserted that he was entitled to credit under Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5 and that denying him credit was an equal protection violation.


OVERVIEW: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus, but allowed him credit for time served in state prison following his return there as an escaped prisoner. Petitioner was serving a prison term for robbery when he escaped. Petitioner was captured in possession of a firearm and heroin. Petitioner was returned to state prison and charges were filed against him in the county court, but were dismissed when charges were filed in municipal court. As part of a plea bargain, the escape charge was dismissed and petitioner pleaded guilty to the drug and weapons charges. The court stated that, in its opinion, petitioner was not entitled to credit for the time served prior to the entry of his plea pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5. The court reasoned that the original robbery conviction was the reason for petitioner's incarceration in state prison, not the pending charges. However, the court conceded that it was obligated to follow precedent that held that petitioner would be entitled to credit. The court denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus because petitioner was not eligible for immediate release, but ordered that the credit be given.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus because he was not eligible for immediate release, but ordered that he be given credit for time served. The court disagreed and stated that there was no equal protection violation and that petitioner was not entitled to credit when his incarceration was the result of prior charges. However, the court was obligated to follow precedent that reached the opposite conclusion.

Hull v. Cason


Civ. Nos. 38801, 40034, 41036.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


88 Cal. App. 3d 768; 151 Cal. Rptr. 438; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2268; 18 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1379; 18 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8920



Dec. 28, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg granted Mar. 28, 1979 (S.F. 24004)
June 19, 1980, cause retrans. to Ct. of App., 1st Dist., Div. 1, for reconsideration in light of Price v. Civil Service Com. (1980) 26 Cal.3d 257, Dothard v. Rawlinson (1977) 433 U.S. 321, 328-332, and Firefighters Institute v. City of St. Louis, Mo. (8th Cir. 1978) 588 F.2d 235, 239-242, cert. den. sub nom. Banta v. Firefighters Insititute (1979) 443 U.S. 904.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, Nos. 451337-451339, Robert K. Barber, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Caucasian firefighters and the city, appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) that granted affirmative relief to plaintiffs, black citizens and firefighters, by imposing a quota for the hiring of minority firefighters and held that the fire department's written examinations, physical standards and tests, and seniority weighting were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a group of black citizens and firefighters, brought a class action against defendant city and contended that the percentage of minorities employed by the fire department bore no reasonable relationship to their percentage in the population and that the fire department's examinations and standards did not substantially relate to the performance of the job. Plaintiffs sought a writ of mandate calculated to dissipate the effect of the fire department's history of discrimination. Caucasians who were fire fighters or who aspired to hold such jobs joined with defendant city as intervenors in defense of plaintiffs' action and contended that their employment or promotion chances would be lost or jeopardized by the affirmative relief sought by plaintiffs. After the trial court granted affirmative relief in the form of a hiring quota for minority applicants, defendant and intervenors appealed. The court held that those entitled to relief under the Civil Rights Act of 1964 were the individual victims of racial discrimination and not members generally of the race discriminated against and that a quota was a form of racial discrimination. The court therefore reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment granting a writ of mandate and establishing a quota for the hiring of minority firefighters. The court held that a quota was itself a form of racial discrimination. In addition, the court held that relief under the civil rights laws was reserved for the individual victims of racial discrimination and did not apply broadly to members of the race discriminated against.

 

1822 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Ventura County Employees' Retirement Association v. Pope


Civ. No. 52616


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


87 Cal. App. 3d 938; 151 Cal. Rptr. 695; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2247



December 28, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified January 22, 1979. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 14, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 59701, Richard C. Heaton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the cause is remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant third party tortfeasor sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Ventura County, (California) in favor of respondent employee's retirement association in its subrogation action, pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 31820, for one-half disability benefits payable to employee injured by appellant. Appellant asserted error in liability determination, statute of limitations, damages, and effect of settlement agreement.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a judgment in favor of respondent employee's retirement association in subrogation action against appellant third party tortfeasor, for one-half the disability benefits payable to injured employee. Employee settled her claim against appellant and executed a general release. The court held that subrogation judgment must be reversed when trial court proceeded under the mistaken impression that liability was conclusively determined by respondent's administrative decision to bring the suit. The court remanded for a new trial, clarifying that appellant could contest liability. The court rejected appellant's arguments that the statute providing for subrogation actions, Cal. Gov't Code § 31820, violated equal protection or due process. The court held that the appropriate statute of limitations for such subrogation actions was the one-year limit of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 340(3), not the three-year limit applied to statutory actions, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 338(1). The court held that settlement agreement was not binding on appellant, but that a correct determination of damages must account for payments respondent would have been obligated to pay to employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of respondent and remanded for a new trial. The court held that judgment was flawed when trial court assumed liability had already been determined. The court stated that appellant could contest liability, that one-year statute of limitations applied, that damages must take into account payments respondent was already obligated to make, and that settlement agreement was not binding.

In re Heidi T.


Civ. No. 42644


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


87 Cal. App. 3d 864; 151 Cal. Rptr. 263; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2238



December 27, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. A 0764, Richard W. Rhodes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) that found appellant's minor children were neglected by appellant and referred the children for adoptive placement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother relinquished physical custody of her two minor children to a juvenile agency. The children were adjudicated dependent and placed in foster care. Psychiatric evidence revealed appellant suffered from a chronic mental illness. The lower court found it would be detrimental to return the children to appellant's custody and rendered judgment free of parental custody, and referred them for adoption. Appellant sought review. There had to be clear and convincing evidence to support permanent severance of a parental relationship. The court limited its determination as to whether substantial evidence existed to support the severance. The court found substantial evidence existed to establish appellant was incapable of providing proper support and control over her children. The report from an investigation was properly admitted into evidence because appellant was given a meaningful opportunity to cross-examine and controvert the content of the report. Appellant's minor children were not entitled to separate counsel to represent their interests because appellant was extended an adequate opportunity to present evidence as to the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that terminated appellant mother's custody of her children and referred them for adoptive placement was affirmed because there was substantial evidence to establish appellant was incapable of providing proper support and control over her children.

Cemetery Board v. Telophase Society of America


Civ. No. 19392


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


87 Cal. App. 3d 847; 151 Cal. Rptr. 248; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2237



December 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 21, 1979. Manuel, J., did not Participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 214623, Lester Van Tatenhove, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cemetery board sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) that found defendant crematory did not perform cremations and was not operating as a cemetery, and denied plaintiff's request to enjoin defendant from performing any cremations without a certificate of authority.


OVERVIEW: Defendant crematory provided simple cremation services. Defendant cremated bodies and the remains were transferred to a separate entity, which scattered the ashes at sea. Defendant's application for a certificate of authority was denied by plaintiff state cemetery board. Plaintiff was a statewide administrative agency charged with administering and enforcing the Cemetery Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 9600 et seq. Plaintiff filed suit to enjoin defendant from performing cremations without a certificate of authority. The trial court found defendant did not perform cremations and was not operating as a cemetery. Plaintiff appealed. The court found defendant was not in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 9768 because it neither made interments nor performed cremations. Defendant was not operating as a cemetery under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 9715. The court affirmed because defendant did not perform cremations or make interments within statutory definition. Because services provided by defendant did not fall within statutory definitions for coverage under Cemetery Act, defendant was not required to have a certificate of authority issued by plaintiff before rendering its services.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that found defendant crematory did not perform cremations and was not operating as a cemetery was affirmed because defendant did not fall within the statutory definitions for coverage under the Cemetery Act.

 

1825 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Heitz v. County of Sacramento


Civ. No. 17186


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


87 Cal. App. 3d 754; 151 Cal. Rptr. 429; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2231



December 22, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 266713, Lawrence K. Karlton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which entered a judgment of dismissal after the trial court sustained defendant county's demurrer without leave to amend his complaint for recovery of damages for injuries resulting from a swine flu immunization received at a defendant's inoculation center.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff resident alleged he was permanently disabled as a consequence of a swine flu immunization he received from defendant county. Defendant responded with a general demurrer asserting total immunity under the provisions of Cal. Gov't Code § 856.6. The trial court granted immunity and plaintiff appealed, asserting that § 856.6 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that § 856.6 was constitutional because it related to and acted uniformly upon the whole of any single class of individuals and the classification was founded upon some natural, intrinsic or constitutional distinction. The court further found that plaintiff lacked standing to claim that § 856.6 fostered economic discrimination because plaintiff's complaint failed to allege inability on his part to obtain inoculation from a private physician and the need to be inoculated through publicly funded clinics. Lastly, the court found that the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, did not require § 856.6 to yield to the federal statute, 42 U.S.C.S. §247b, because the federal statute expressly set forth the exclusive nature of a claimant's remedy for injury under the National Swine Flu Immunization Program.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of dismissal and judgment giving defendant county immunity from plaintiff resident's action seeking damages for injury sustained when he received an immunization from defendant was affirmed because the state immunity statute was constitutional, plaintiff lacked standing to claim that the statute fostered economic discrimination, and the statute was not invalidated by a corresponding federal statute.

Kaiser Foundation Hospitals v. Workers' Compensation Appeals Board


Civ. Nos. 50512, 50671, 50798, 50921


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


87 Cal. App. 3d 336; 151 Cal. Rptr. 368; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2188; 43 Cal. Comp. Cases 1300



December 15, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions of Respondents Smith, Workers' Compensation Appeals Board and Industrial Indemnity Company for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied February 14, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Because, for the reasons above set forth under rubric II, the procedure followed by the board in all four cases denied Kaiser due process of law, the awards are annulled and the cases are remanded to the board for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. In the Smith case (Civ. No. 50921) the board shall determine whether, applying the standards herein set forth, industrial causation was actually in issue when the compromise was tendered for approval. In all four cases Kaiser or the employer may litigate any dispute over the gross amount of its legitimate claim.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospitals sought review of a decision from respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California) that reduced the amount of their liens for services against the claims settlements of respondent workers pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 4903.1(c).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner hospitals contended that respondent Workers' Compensation Insurance Board had improperly reduced the amounts of its liens against the settlements of respondent workers. Respondent board found in favor of respondent workers. On appeal, petitioners contended that respondent board's retroactive application of Cal. Lab. Code § 4903.1(c) was improper, that the statute was unconstitutionally vague, and that it was denied equal protection of the laws. The court found that the statute was not applied retroactively because petitioners' rights in the liens vested after the statute's effective date at the time of settlement. The court ruled that the statute was not vague but that respondent workers had not complied with due process requirements because petitioners were not served with sufficient documentary evidence supporting the basis for the reductions. The court held that the reduction of the claim where the cause of a respondent worker's injury was not at issue denied petitioners equal protection of the laws because the employer was required to pay the full value of the services provided. Thus, the court annulled the awards and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the awards to respondent workers and remanded the matters back to respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board for further proceedings. The court held that due process required respondent workers to advise petitioner hospitals of evidence in support of the reduction in the amount of petitioners' liens prior to the settlement of the claims.

Ghafari v. Mun. Court for San Francisco Judicial Dist.


Civ. Nos. 41690, 41695


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


87 Cal. App. 3d 255; 150 Cal. Rptr. 813; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2180; 2 A.L.R.4th 1230



December 14, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of the Real Party in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 14, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Nos. 718409 and 717174, Francis McCarty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The orders are reversed and the causes remanded with directions to issue the writs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of the Iranian Students' Association (ISA), sought review of an order from respondent Municipal Court for the San Francisco Judicial District of the City and County of San Francisco denying their petition for a writ of prohibition after they were arrested for violating Cal. Penal Code § 650.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were members of the Iranian Students' Association (ISA). They were arrested for violating Cal. Penal Code § 650 on the ground that they were picketing in disguise by placing leaflets between their glasses and face. Appellants explained that they were fearful that if their identity became known, retaliatory measures would be taken against them by agents of the Iranian government. Appellants petitioned respondent municipal court for a writ of prohibition. Respondent denied their petitions. On appeal, the court granted appellants' petitions and reversed and remanded respondent's order, finding that § 650 was unconstitutional because it was overbroad, vague, and denied equal protection of the laws. The statute was overbroad on its face because it flatly prohibited anonymity under circumstances where protected activities were involved, and because the restriction was not required by a compelling state interest nor was it implemented in the least restrictive manner possible. The statute swept too broadly by flatly prohibiting anonymous public appearances by persons exercising their First Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellants' petition for a writ of prohibition was reversed and remanded because the state statute under which appellants were arrested was unconstitutional because it was overbroad, vague, and denied equal protection of the laws.

People v. Saffell

COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE

1829 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shults


Crim. Nos. 18296, 18297, 18298


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


87 Cal. App. 3d 101; 150 Cal. Rptr. 747; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2161



December 7, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 5, 1979, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the Southern Judicial District of San Mateo County, Nos. A-838943, A-838938, 130-M-48, AD 959, AD 960, and AD 953, Norman J. Gatzert and David Pomerenk, Referees.



DISPOSITION: The judgment as to the November 5, 1976, offense is reversed. The judgments as to the June 6 and June 7, 1977, offenses are reversed and remanded for a determination of whether appellant had suffered three prior infraction convictions within twelve months of the commission of the fourth offense. If such convictions have not been suffered, the judgment is reinstated and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Municipal Court for the Southern Judicial District of San Mateo County (California) of three traffic infractions. He sought reversal, arguing that the traffic referee denied him his statutory right to a jury trial under Cal. Veh. Code § 40000.28, where he offered to admit in each of the three cases to three prior infractions with a 12-month period.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with three traffic infractions. In all three cases, he offered to admit three prior infractions within a 12-month period, and requested a jury trial. The traffic referee denied the request, the citations were tried without a jury, and appellant was found guilty. In one case, a misdemeanor complaint was filed but respondent filed a motion to strike the priors and the motion was granted. Appellant sought review, arguing that under Cal. Veh. Code § 40000.28, he had a statutory right to a jury trial. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that permitting appellant to elevate the charge to a misdemeanor did not unconstitutionally subject respondent's exclusive responsibility for criminal prosecution to a private citizen, Cal. Const. art. V, § 13, and that other statutes provided a defendant the right to increase the seriousness of the charge, Cal. Penal Code § 17(b). The court held that the municipal court's decision to strike the prior in the third case without having provided its reasons required reversal, because the municipal court could not deprive appellant of his right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's convictions for three traffic infractions. The court held that under the California Vehicle Code, appellant had a statutory right to elevate the traffic infraction to a misdemeanor charge by admitting prior infractions not charged.

 

1830 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


St. John v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 20037


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


87 Cal. App. 3d 30; 150 Cal. Rptr. 697; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2156



December 5, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons hereinabove set forth, the peremptory writ should issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, Orange County Clerk and ex officio clerk of respondent Superior Court of Orange County (California), sought a peremptory writ of mandate to compel respondent superior court to vacate its adoption of, and to refrain from implementing, a court rule which, pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 69898(c), (d), transferred certain court-related duties performed by petitioner to respondent's executive officer.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a county clerk and ex officio clerk of respondent superior court in the same county, sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent to vacate a court rule, adopted pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 69898 (c), (d), which transferred all of petitioner's superior court-related functions to respondent's executive officer. Petitioner argued that Cal. Gov't Code § 69898 (c), (d) was unconstitutional in light of Cal. Const. art. VI, § 4, which made a county clerk also the superior court clerk, ex officio. The court held Cal. Gov't Code § 69898 was constitutional because it did not diminish or destroy the constitutional office of superior court clerk. However, the court also held that the challenged court rule exceeded the authority granted by the statute because it purported to transfer to the superior court executive officer all of the powers and duties exercised by the county clerk in connection with judicial matters; not in his capacity as county clerk as the statute specified, but in his capacity as clerk of the superior court. The court held that the rule if implemented would have the impermissible effect of abolishing an office established by Cal. Const. art. VI, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate because the court rule challenged by petitioner, a county clerk and ex officio court clerk of respondent superior court, would have the effect, if implemented, of destroying the constitutional office of superior court clerk.

 

1831 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


San Francisco Labor Council v. University of California


Civ. No. 41756.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


86 Cal. App. 3d 863; 150 Cal. Rptr. 671; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2135



Dec. 1, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Feb. 14, 1979 (see 26 C.3d 785)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 712768, John E. Benson, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant labor council and related parties challenged the judgment of a California trial court, which refused to order respondent university regents to comply with Cal. Educ. Code § 92611 as to wages paid to laborers, workmen, and mechanics because it was unconstitutional. The appellate court granted rehearing to reexamine the constitutional questions and to clarify its reasoning.


OVERVIEW: Appellant labor council and related parties filed a petition seeking to mandate respondent university regents to comply with Cal. Educ. Code § 92611 in giving consideration to local general prevailing rates of wages for laborers, workmen, and mechanics employed on an hourly or per diem basis in fixing minimum salary limits for respondent's comparable employees. Upon demurrer, it was stipulated that the only issue to be determined was the constitutionality of § 92611. In sustaining respondent's demurrer without leave to amend, the trial court found § 92611 unconstitutional. The court reversed and held that the enactment of § 92611 as a matter of statewide concern was a valid exercise of the legislative power. The court further held that the public interest in the establishment of a uniform minimum wage standard to be considered in fixing salary levels for the identified class was of sufficient importance to justify legislative regulation as a matter of statewide concern. Additionally, the court found that § 92611 did not conflict with the provisions of Cal. Const. art. IX, § 9(a), (f).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision not to order respondent university regents to comply with statutory requirements as to wages paid to laborers, workmen, and mechanics because the statutory requirements did not conflict with the California Constitution. The court remanded for further proceedings on the petition for writ of mandate filed by appellant labor council and related parties.

 

1832 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Uneedus v. California Shoppers, Inc.


Civ. No. 19570


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


86 Cal. App. 3d 932; 150 Cal. Rptr. 596; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2141; 1979-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P62,845



December 1, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified December 14, 1978. A petition for a rehearing was denied December 21, 1978, and respondents' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied February 21, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. 112236, John H. Hews, Judge.



DISPOSITION: In sum then, it is our view that the proper application of section 17082 to the case proved by plaintiff entitles it to three times the damages awarded. In so holding, we are doing nothing more nor less than following the federal decisions which apply federal statutes similar in content and purpose to the California statute here under consideration. The judgment is ordered modified accordingly. As thus modified, the judgment is affirmed. However, plaintiff shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a California corporation that published a weekly advertising newspaper, challenged the order of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which awarded it general damages and attorney's fees under the California Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§17000- 17208 but denied plaintiff's request for treble damages claimed under § 17082 of the act.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a California corporation, published a weekly advertising newspaper. Defendant, a California corporation and various individuals, began distribution of a similar advertising newspaper in the communities where plaintiff distributed its paper, offering, without charge, display ad space and also selling such space below actual cost. Plaintiff sought damages and injunctive relief alleging defendant had violated various sections of the California Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§17000- 17208. The trial court awarded plaintiff the relief it sought, except that it denied statutory treble damages because it found that defendants' acts were not malicious. In this case of first impression, the court held that the trial court erred in refusing to award treble damages. The court held that because plaintiff had proved actual damages under the California Unfair Practices Act, it was entitled to mandatory treble damages pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17082. Analogizing from the federal Robinson-Patman Act, 15 U.S.C. § 13, which provided for mandatory treble damages, the court held that the issue of whether defendant acted maliciously was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment because plaintiff newspaper publisher's proof of general damages entitled it to three times the damages awarded under the California Unfair Practices Act. Thus, the court affirmed the judgment as modified.

Sallas v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 42429


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


86 Cal. App. 3d 737; 150 Cal. Rptr. 543; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2119



November 28, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 494824-5, Harold B. Hove, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the superior court is reversed. That court will take further proceedings not inconsistent with our holding and the opinions we have expressed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants petitioned respondent Superior Court of Alameda County (California) for a writ of prohibition seeking to enjoin the municipal court, which overruled their demurrers, from further proceeding with their prosecution for unlawfully using a controlled substance, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11550. Respondent denied the petition and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged in the municipal court with unlawfully using a controlled substance, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11550. The substance was unnamed. The municipal court overruled appellants' demurrers, arguing that the facts stated did not provide notice of the offense, Cal. Penal Code § 952. Respondent superior court denied appellants' request for a writ of prohibition to enjoin the proceedings. Appellants sought review. The court reversed, holding that the complaints denied appellants' due process of law, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because appellants were not reasonably advised on the charges against them, given a fair opportunity to prepare their defense, or able to avoid surprise at trial. The court found that § 11550 proscribed the use of 120 drugs, that prompt discovery did not satisfy due process rights, that criminal discovery was inadequate, that § 11550 comported with equal protection requirements, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, that identification of only the drugs' class could be sufficient, and the mandatory 90-day minimum jail confinement for the statute's violators was not cruel and unusual punishment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of respondent superior court which denied appellants' petition for writ of mandate to enjoin the municipal court from further proceeding with appellants' prosecution for unlawful use of a controlled substance. The court held that the failure of the complaints to identify in any way the controlled substance denied appellants due process of law.

In re C.


Civ. No. 3784.


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 3d 603; 150 Cal. Rptr. 356; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2107



Nov. 21, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Jan. 17, 1979 (S.F. 23978)
Jan. 17, 1980, cause retrans to Ct. of App., 5th Dist., for reconsideration in light of In Re Eric J. (1979) 25 Cal.3d 522. See 104 C.A.3d 16 


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 43619, Joseph F. Noriega, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which adjudged appellant a ward of the court and committed appellant to the youth authority for the longest of three time periods specified for adults under Cal. Penal Code § 1170, without a finding of aggravating circumstances as required for adults under § 1170.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found to be a person within Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, in that appellant committed forgery, a felony under Cal. Penal Code § 470, battery against a peace officer, a felony under Cal. Penal Code § 243, and resisting an officer, a misdemeanor under Cal. Penal Code § 148. The juvenile court committed appellant to the youth authority for three years on the felonies without a determination that there were circumstances in aggravation. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the sentence on appellant, three years, was a greater period than what would have been imposed upon an adult who had committed the same offense. The court held that parole was a restraint of liberty and that the sentencing scheme whereby a juvenile could be confined for a potential period longer than an adult that committed the same offense violated the Equal Protection clauses of the California Constitution and The United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's sentence because appellant was subject to a period of potential confinement longer than an adult would have been that committed the same offense, and therefore it violated the Equal Protection clauses of the California and United States Constitution. The cause was remanded for a new sentencing hearing with direction for the trial court to follow the sentencing rules used for similarly situated adults.

TRIM, Inc. v. County of Monterey


Civ. No. 41138


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


86 Cal. App. 3d 539; 150 Cal. Rptr. 351; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2100



November 21, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Monterey County, No. 72339, Ralph M. Drummond, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is reversed with directions to sustain respondents' demurrer with leave for appellant to amend its complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit taxpayer corporation challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which sustained a demurrer without leave to amend appellant's complaint under Cal. Civ. Proc. §526(a) on behalf of respondents, County of Monterey and tax assessor of Monterey County.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nonprofit taxpayer corporation alleged that respondents, County of Monterey and tax assessor of Monterey County, assessed some property at substantially less than the fair market value and sought injunctive relief and damages under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 526(a). The trial court sustained respondents' demurrer without leave to amend the complaint. On appeal, the court concluded that appellant's allegations did not state a cause of action under § 526(a). While § 526(a) allowed appellants to challenge wasteful expenditure of county funds by respondents, the court found that the unequal assessment practices of respondents were not waste within the meaning of § 526(a). Appellant's relief was for mandamus that required respondents to assess the property in accordance with Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1, and Cal Rev. & Tax. Code §401, et seq. Thus, the court reversed with directions to sustain respondents' demurrer with leave for appellant to amend its complaint to allege that the manner of assessing property in the county violated the statutory mandate that all property be assessed at a specified percentage of its fair market or full value.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the demurrer of respondents, County of Monterey and Monterey County tax assessor, because unequal assessment practices were not waste. The court held that appellant nonprofit taxpayer corporation should have been allowed to amend its complaint seeking mandamus requiring respondents to assess property in accordance to statutory mandates requiring that all property be assessed at the same percentage.
