In re J.


Civ. No. 18082.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


86 Cal. App. 3d 513; 150 Cal. Rptr. 299; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2098



November 17, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] as modified Dec. 5, 1978
Hg. granted Jan. 17, 1979 (see 25 C.3d 522)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. Juv. 90494, Richard L. Vaughn, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from a dispositional order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which committed him to the California Youth Authority for the maximum term of confinement permitted by law after a finding that he had committed a burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was declared a ward of the juvenile court pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, after he was found to have committed a burglary. Defendant was committed to the California Youth Authority (CYA) for the maximum term of confinement permitted by law. Defendant appealed and contended that the statutory scheme of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 726, 731, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new dispositional hearing. The court held the provision within § 726 relating to the automatic imposition of the upper term of confinement violated the Equal protection clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Cal. Const., art. I, § 7(a), because it treated similarly situated juveniles differently than adults for whom no automatic imposition was required. The court held that juvenile courts would now have to apply the substantive rule of Cal. Penal Code § 1170(d), which provided for the sentencing of the middle term unless aggravating or mitigating circumstances were established. The court also held the trial court erred in failing to give defendant credit for time spent in custody pending juvenile court proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new disposition hearing because the automatic sentencing provisions of the juvenile statute violated the Equal Protection clause and were unconstitutional. The court held that juvenile courts should follow the penal code, which called for imposition of a middle term unless aggravating or mitigating circumstances were found, and ordered that defendant juvenile receive credit for pre-disposition time served.

Perry Farms, Inc. v. Agricultural Labor Relations Bd.


Civ. No. 17800


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 3d 448; 150 Cal. Rptr. 495; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2092; 88 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,218

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied December 13, 1978, and the petitions of the real party in interest and petitioners for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied January 24, 1979. OVERVIEW: Real party in interest labor union was certified as the collective bargaining agent of agricultural workers employed by petitioners, agricultural employers. Wagner v. State of California


Civ. No. 16017


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 3d 922; 150 Cal. Rptr. 489; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2140



November 6, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 30, 1978, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied January 3, 1979.

DISPOSITION: The judgment in favor of the State is reversed; the judgment in favor of Spink is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver appealed an order from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sustained respondents state and corporation's demurrers dismissing appellant's cross-complaint for negligence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver filed a cross-complaint against respondents state and corporation for the negligent design, plan and construction of an intersection where a car accident occurred resulting in a personal injury suit against appellant. Appellant sought contribution from respondents, in the event appellant was found liable in the personal injury suit. Respondent state demurred citing sovereign immunity and respondent corporation demurred claiming the statute of limitations had run on the action. The lower court sustained respondents' demurrers and dismissed appellant's actions. On appeal, the court reversed in part because sovereign immunity was inapplicable as an injury was caused by a dangerous condition of the government's property and appellant could join respondent state as a tortfeasor and if necessary obtain partial indemnity by cross-complaint. The court affirmed in part, finding the statute of limitations in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 337.1 was not unconstitutional and had run on appellant's cause against respondent corporation as appellant alleged a patent defect and brought the claim after four years from completion of the construction of the intersection.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining demurrers and dismissing appellant driver's cross-complaint for negligence was reversed as to respondent state on the grounds that respondent state could be joined as a tortfeasor for partial indemnity and sovereign immunity did not apply, and was affirmed as to respondent corporation as the statute of limitations had run on appellant's claim.

People v. McDaniel


Crim. No. 3293.


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 3d 109; 150 Cal. Rptr. 52; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2054



Nov. 3, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Jan. 17, 1979 (see 24 C.3d 661)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Madera County, No. 4388, Jack L. Hammerberg, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Madera County (California), which convicted defendant of violating Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11355, after instructing the jury on a modified application of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was brought to trial on the basis that he violated Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11355 when he offered to sell and deliver a controlled substance to an undercover officer. Defendant was arrested prior to the delivery and he did not possess a controlled substance as stipulated. Defendant sought an acquittal based on the absence of evidence of an actual transfer of a non-controlled substance between defendant and the officer, which the lower court denied and instructed the jury that an offer to sell a controlled substance followed by an offer to deliver a non-controlled substance was a crime. On appeal, the court held that despite the plain meaning of the statute, it was not sufficient to merely offer to make a delivery of a substitute and that the statute's historical application required an overt, direct and unequivocal activity directed toward a physical transfer of a specific and identified substance. As the lower court's instructions permitted a guilty verdict even when the delivery requirement was not proved, the court found that an essential element of the crime was omitted from the instructions and reversed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant's acquittal was reversed on the grounds that the lower court erred in instructing the jury to find defendant guilty on the basis that defendant offered to sell a controlled substance and offered to deliver a substitute, even though the act of delivery was an essential element of the crime charged.

 

1841 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Pacific Diamond Co. v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 43602


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 3d 871; 149 Cal. Rptr. 813; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2027



October 27, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioners' application for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 20, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, insofar as the trial court held California law applicable in its order of November 3, 1977, the trial court is directed to set aside its order and the cause is remanded to the trial court for such further proceedings as may be appropriate and not inconsistent with views expressed herein. Real party in interest to have his costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, diamond corporation and president, sought a writ of mandate against respondent the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California)'s order that held that California law was applicable to determine the liability of real party in interest hotel for damages from a diamond robbery, where real party in interest and the robbery were in Colorado.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner president of petitioner diamond corporation, a California corporation, stayed in real party in interest hotel, which was located in Colorado. Petitioner president temporarily placed diamonds in real party in interest's safety deposit box and was robbed after he removed them. Petitioners filed an action for damages, and respondent superior court held that California law applied, which law limited real party in interest's liability. The court granted petitioners' request for a writ of mandate and held that where a choice of law question existed, the determination was made by applying a governmental interest analysis. The court held that California's governmental interest was to protect the innkeeper within its territorial jurisdiction against unlimited liability and that it had no interest in limiting the liability of a hotel outside its territorial limits. Colorado had a valid governmental interest to see that its innkeeper statutes were applied to hotels situated within its territorial boundaries. The court held that Colorado law was rationally related to its governmental interests, that there were no constitutional violations, and that Colorado law was to be applied.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandate against respondent superior court's order that California law applied to petitioners', diamond corporation and president, for damages and held that California law was not applicable because Colorado had a valid governmental interest in seeing that its innkeeper statutes were applied to inns or hotels situated within its territorial boundaries.

 

1842 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Carson Bulletin


Civ. No. 53293


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 3d 785; 149 Cal. Rptr. 764; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2022



October 25, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 173983, Alfred L. Margolis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified to delete the requirement of special notice to the City of Carson. As modified, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper publisher challenged a judgment, entered by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which vacated a prior judgment adjudicating appellant's newspaper as one of general circulation in and around respondent city.


OVERVIEW: Appellant newspaper publisher received a judgment that established his newspaper as one of general circulation in and around respondent city. Thereafter, the trial court granted respondent's motion to vacate that judgment. Review was sought by appellant. The court held that the motion to vacate was properly granted. The court stated that appellant's paper could not qualify as one of general circulation under Cal. Gov't Code § 6000 because it was not published within the boundaries of respondent. The court rejected appellant's contention that Cal. Gov't Code § 6008 was unconstitutional because the term "substantial" was vague. The court stated that the meaning of "substantial" could be easily ascertained by making reference to other definable sources, such as dictionaries. The court held that the handful of subscribers to appellant's paper within the respondent's boundaries was not a "substantial distribution of paid subscribers," the requirement of § 6008 for a finding of general circulation. The court set aside a special notice requirement imposed on appellant in future actions under §§ 6000, 6008.


OUTCOME: The court deleted the requirement that appellant newspaper publisher notify respondent city of any future action to have his paper declared one of general circulation. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed because a requirement that a paper have a substantial distribution of paid subscribers, in order to qualify as one of general circulation, was not constitutionally vague, and appellant's paper lacked the needed distribution.

Zee Toys, Inc. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. Nos. 52977, 53695, 53306


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 3d 763; 149 Cal. Rptr. 750; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2021



October 25, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' petitions for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied January 17, 1979. Mosk, J., Richardson, J., and Manuel, J., were of the opinion that the petitions should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. C179151 and C191156, Jack T. Ryburn and Campbell M. Lucas, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are reversed and both causes remanded to the trial court which is directed to enter judgments in favor of defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county and cities, appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff importers in a consolidated action for a refund of ad valorem taxes paid under protest pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 225, 225.1.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff importers filed separate actions, which were consolidated, against defendants, county and cities, protesting and claiming an exemption under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 225, 225.1 from the payment of an ad valorem taxes levied on tangible personal property stored in the state. Plaintiffs paid the taxes under protest and sought refunds. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, holding that plaintiffs were exempted from payment of the ad valorem tax under §§ 225, 225.1. Defendants appealed, contending that §§ 225, 225.1 were unconstitutional under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl.3. Plaintiffs countered that the exemptions were valid or, alternatively, that defendants lacked standing. The court reversed the lower court's judgment, holding that §§ 225, 225.1 violated the constitution because they interfered with Congress's power over commerce in exempting foreign goods from ad valorem taxes without extending the same protection to interstate goods. The court further held that defendants had standing because defendants had sufficient stake in the outcome of the litigation to vigorously pursue the claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which granted summary judgment to plaintiff importers in an action for refunds of ad valorem taxes, and directed that judgment be entered for defendants, county and cities. The court held that, under state law, plaintiff's property was exempted as foreign goods from taxation where interstate goods were not exempted, thus, the state law violated the federal constitution.

Crawford v. Herringer


Civ. No. 42275


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


85 Cal. App. 3d 544; 149 Cal. Rptr. 578; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2001



October 16, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 15, 1978, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 13, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 712028, John E. Benson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court judgment is affirmed. 6



6 Note that under the recent Supreme Court decision in Addison v. State of California (1978) 21 Cal.3d 313 [146 Cal.Rptr. 224, 578 P.2d 941], and cases cited therein appellant may obtain the benefit of equitable tolling of the statute of limitations if he files another action in the municipal court raising these issues. Since the dismissal was for lack of jurisdiction, the doctrine of res judicata will not prevent appellant from filing another complaint in the proper forum. (See 4 Witkin, Cal. Procedure (2d ed. 1971) §§ 173-175, pp. 3315-3318.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed his cause of action for reimbursement of improperly assessed election pamphlet costs against respondent rapid transit district on the sustaining of respondent's demurrer to appellant's third-amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: Appellant candidate challenged by means of an action to recover moneys paid the assessment of costs for the election pamphlets published by respondent rapid transit district. Respondent demurred to appellant's cause of action on the basis that the superior court lacked jurisdiction, the demurrer was sustained and the complaint dismissed, and appellant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal and held that if the action involved the legality of a tax, import, assessment, toll, or municipal fine, it was within the superior court's jurisdiction; but where, as here, the contested costs were for the specific purpose of reimbursing the public utility for a service rendered, were not routinely levied, and were limited to the public entity's expenses, the charges were not normal taxes, imposts, or assessments and did not raise issues of statewide importance in the interpretation of the statute and the legality of the levy. Thus, the court concluded, the superior court was without jurisdiction over appellant's complaint, and respondent's demurrer was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant candidate's cause of action for recovery of improperly assessed election pamphlet costs on respondent rapid transit district's demurrer was affirmed because the case did not involve tax issues of state-wide importance, thus the trial court lacked jurisdiction and the matter should have been filed in municipal court.

CBS, Inc. v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 43117


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


85 Cal. App. 3d 241; 149 Cal. Rptr. 421; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1966; 4 Media L. Rep. 1568



October 2, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 30, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the peremptory writ is denied, the alternative writ is discharged, and the matter is remanded with instructions that the court reconsider the scope of its order, having in mind that the legitimate needs of law enforcement and CBS's claimed pledge of secrecy might both be preserved if the discovery order were narrowed by appropriate editing of the video tapes in question.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner television network sought a writ of prohibition to set aside the order of respondent Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which denied petitioner's motion to quash the real parties' in interest subpoena for media materials depicting meetings between the real parties in interest and narcotics officers compiled by petitioner as part of a television program.


OVERVIEW: Real parties in interest, were charged with selling a controlled substance in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11379, and caused a subpoena duces tecum to be issued and served on petitioner television network to discover certain videotapes, tape recordings, and motion pictures of meetings between the real parties in interest and narcotics officers compiled by petitioner to be broadcast during its television program. Respondent superior court denied petitioner's motion to quash and ordered that petitioner deliver all such media materials to the real parties in interest. Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition commanding respondent to set aside its order. The court denied the peremptory writ, finding that Cal. Evid. Code § 1070 did not apply where confidentiality was no longer an issue. The court remanded to respondent to reconsider the scope of its order. Respondent's order was impermissibly broad because respondent never viewed the requested materials. The voice tapes of the meetings may have been sufficient, and if all the materials were deemed necessary to real parties' defense, the faces of exposed undercover officers could have been blocked-out.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner television network's peremptory writ and remanded to respondent superior court for reconsideration of the scope of its order because order was impermissibly broad and could have been narrowed had respondent viewed the media materials.

In re Gray


Crim. No. 18071


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


85 Cal. App. 3d 255; 149 Cal. Rptr. 416; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1967



October 2, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 1, 1978, and respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 30, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Monterey County, No. HC 505, D. Richard Barelli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of February 28, 1978, granting the writ of habeas corpus, is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order granting habeas corpus to petitioner by the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which ordered the Community Release Board to conduct a second serious offender hearing pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2(b) to redetermine petitioner's sentence term.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty in two cases to robbery in the first degree, and was sentenced in each case under the Indeterminate Sentence Law to five years in prison, to run concurrently. At a subsequent serious offender hearing, the Community Release Board (CRB) imposed an additional 12-month term to petitioner's sentence under the Determinate Sentencing Act (DSA), pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2(a). On appeal by the state, following the trial court's issuance of writ of habeas corpus to petitioner, the court reversed the writ and found that the CRB had the authority under the DSA to impose the additional period. The court determined that the express language of Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2(b) specifically authorized the CRB to increase the base term, in accordance with the formula set forth in § 1170.2(a), due to the number of crimes of which petitioner was convicted The court found that the authority granted to the CRB by the legislature was not an unlawful delegation of judicial function to the executive branch because the CRB's recalculation of the term was not a resentencing but rather a means to achieve the legislative objective of uniform treatment of offenders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the writ of habeas corpus issued to petitioner by the trial court because the Community Release Board was specifically authorized by the legislature to impose additional penalty to petitioner's sentence pursuant to the Determinate Sentencing Act.

 

1847 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Department of General Services v. Superior Court


Civ. Nos. 17573, 17574


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


85 Cal. App. 3d 273; 147 Cal. Rptr. 422; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1969



October 2, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a peremptory writ issue ordering respondeat superior court to vacate its order of January 26, 1978, granting real parties' motion for summary judgment in superior court case number 265006 and to enter instead an order denying the motion. The alternative writs, having served their purpose, are discharged. Petitioners are to recover their costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Joint Rules Committee of the California Legislature and other agencies restoring the state capitol, filed a writ of mandamus seeking to have vacated an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted a motion for summary judgment to the Sacramento Builders' Exchange, real parties in interest.


OVERVIEW: A minority business enterprise participation plan was implemented in the restoration project of the state capitol, requiring that any subcontract proposal exceeding $ 250,000 would have to commit at least 20 percent of its total dollar value to a minority-owned business in order to be eligible for consideration. Real parties, the Sacramento Builders' Exchange, filed an action to enjoin this requirement on grounds that the provision violated competitive bidding requirements applicable to the capitol restoration project and violated the equal protection and due process guarantees of the California and United States constitutions. The trial court granted real parties' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court granted a peremptory writ ordering the trial court to vacate its order and to instead enter an order denying real parties' motion for summary judgment. The court held that there were triable issues of fact regarding equal protection in the imposition of the racial quota, and required that on remand the relevant inquiry be whether the racial quota passed the strict scrutiny standard of review.


OUTCOME: The court granted a peremptory writ ordering the trial court to vacate its order, and to instead enter an order denying the motion for summary judgment of real parties in interest, the Sacramento Builders' Exchange, because there were triable issues of fact regarding equal protection in the imposition of the racial quota, and the relevant inquiry on remand would be whether the racial quota passed the strict scrutiny standard of review.

 

1848 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


City of Los Angeles v. Superior Court


Civ. Nos. 48770, 50055


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


85 Cal. App. 3d 143; 149 Cal. Rptr. 320; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1956



September 27, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C81867, Philip Saeta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The petition for a peremptory writ of mandate is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real party in interest appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, County of Los Angeles and its employees, and denied summary judgment in favor of defendants, City of Los Angeles and its employees, in plaintiff's state action seeking damages for the seizure, withholding, and loss of personal property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, real party in interest, brought a state action against defendants, City and County of Los Angeles and certain of their employees, seeking damages for seizure, withholding, and loss of personal property. The court affirmed summary judgment for defendant county and its employees and granted a petition for a peremptory writ of mandate for defendant city and its employees. The court found that plaintiff was not estopped by a jury verdict in a previous federal civil rights action because the verdict in favor of defendants could have been based on a finding that plaintiff had not proved knowledge or intent to violate his civil rights. Although the verdict did not bar plaintiff's case, the court held that plaintiff's action was barred by the previous federal action because plaintiff had attempted to split a single cause of action. The federal action was designed to vindicate the same primary right plaintiff sought in the state action, his interests in the personal property converted and withheld by defendants. The court concluded that the federal action must have been decided on the merits because no procedural issues were raised in that action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendant county and its employees and granted a petition for a peremptory writ of mandate for defendant city and its employees. The court held that the action of plaintiff real party in interest was barred by a previous federal action decided on the merits, because plaintiff had attempted to split a single cause of action and vindicate the same primary right in both suits.

 

1849 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


San Francisco v. Pacello


Civ. No. 41280


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


85 Cal. App. 3d 637; 149 Cal. Rptr. 705; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2010



September 27, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 704124, Charles F. Peery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city and county, sought review of a judgment in favor of defendant homeowners by the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), in a public nuisance abatement action that held plaintiffs' suit was barred by the doctrine of laches. Plaintiffs had filed suit to challenge a decision by the board of permit appeals that found defendant's two-unit property was entitled to a building permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant homeowners appealed to the city and county board of permit appeals, concerning a decision by plaintiffs, city and county, denying defendants a building permit to do work on their two-unit residence. The board overruled plaintiffs' decision and found that defendants had owned and used the property as a two-unit residence for over thirty years, and that plaintiffs were aware of the use, requiring that plaintiffs issue a permit. Plaintiffs challenged that decision and the trial court held that plaintiffs' action against defendants was barred by the doctrine of laches. Plaintiffs challenged that decision on the basis that the board did not have jurisdiction over the matter. The court held that the board did have jurisdiction under the powers granted by the San Francisco City Charter and that it properly ruled on the matter. The court also found that plaintiffs' claim was barred by the doctrine of laches because plaintiffs waited a long time after the board's decision to appeal and that the delay in bringing the action against defendants was prejudicial to them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendant homeowners which found that the action brought by plaintiffs, city and county, was barred by the doctrine of laches. The court ruled that the board did have jurisdiction in which to decide the matter and that the delay by plaintiffs in appealing the board's decision constituted laches that unfairly prejudiced defendants.

 

1850 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nelson


Crim. No. 9545


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


85 Cal. App. 3d 99; 149 Cal. Rptr. 177; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1952



September 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 13, 1978. Bird, C. J., Tobriner, J., and Manuel, J., did not participate therein. Taylor, J., * Elkington, J., * and Kane, J., * participated therein.


* Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Nos. 51982, 51983 and 51984, John M. Sapunor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the sentence given by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), for his guilty pleas to five counts of robbery under Cal. Penal Code § 211, each with use of a firearm under Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5, and one count of assault with a deadly weapon under Cal. Penal Code § 245, with use of a firearm. The trial court found aggravated circumstances and imposed the upper term of imprisonment as to each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to five counts of robbery under Cal. Penal Code § 211, each with use of a firearm under Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5, and one count of assault with a deadly weapon under Cal. Penal Code § 245, with use of a firearm. The trial court imposed the upper term of imprisonment as to each of the counts under Cal. Penal Code §§ 213, 245. Defendant sought review of his sentencing because the trial court had used a preponderance of the evidence standard in deciding the aggravating circumstances that led to an enhanced sentence. Defendant argued that the standard used should have been that of beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed the enhanced sentence and the trial court's use of the preponderance standard under Cal. R. Ct. 439(b), holding that when defendant pled guilty to the offenses and the enhancements, he gave up his right to the use of the higher standard of beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that this was not a violation of due process of the law, because defendant had the right to a trial in which the higher standard would have been used.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment by the trial court to sentence defendant to the upper term of imprisonment for each count to which he pled guilty, for it was permissible to impose such terms upon the findings of aggravated circumstances by a preponderance of the evidence rather than beyond a reasonable doubt, because defendant could have requested a trial and not plead guilty.

 

1851 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Hiatt v. Berkeley


Civ. No. 39033.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


85 Cal. App. 3d 29; 149 Cal. Rptr. 155; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1946; 18 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 233; 18 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8712



Sept. 25, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehg. granted Oct. 25, 1978 (see 88 C.A.3d 503)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 453459-2, Lyle E. Cook, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, council, and officials, challenged an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), awarding damages to respondent city employees on their claim that appellants' affirmative action program violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e et seq., and enjoining enforcement of certain provisions of the program. Respondents challenged the court's denial of attorney's fees and the promotion of two respondents.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city employees challenged an affirmative action program (AAP) that set up racial quotas in hiring and promoting city employees instituted by appellants, city, council, and officials. Affirming the trial court's decision that AAP violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, and title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e et seq., the court held that the racial classifications failed to pass strict scrutiny. The court found that the quotas were not warranted by a compelling governmental interest and the procedures were not necessary to implement the interest. The court reasoned that the establishment of racial quotas was not necessary because the city had no history of discriminatory employment practices. The court reversed the denial of attorney's fees, holding that the trial court should have determined the propriety and amount of attorney's fees because they were expressly provided for in 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e-5k. The court found that the trial court's refusal to issue a writ of mandamus was proper because ordering the promotion of respondents would have been equivalent to mandating the exercise of discretion in a particular manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision awarding damages to respondent city employees because the affirmative action program of appellants city, council, and officials made racial classifications that were not necessary for a compelling governmental interest. The court also affirmed the denial of a writ of mandamus ordering the promotion of two respondents and reversed the denial of attorney's fees because they were specifically authorized by statute.

 

1852 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. State of California


Civ. No. 16386


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


85 Cal. App. 3d 430; 149 Cal. Rptr. 519; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1985



September 22, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 15, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 382460, Louis M. Welsh, and Douglas R. Woodworth, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant victim's father sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which sustained respondent state and its employees' demurrer without leave to amend, in an action brought by appellant alleging that respondents were responsible for his daughter's death because they negligently paroled and failed to supervise the inmate that killed appellant's daughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father filed an action against respondent state and its employees after his daughter was killed by a parolee, alleging, among other things, that respondents negligently paroled the inmate, failed to supervise him, and violated the Civil Rights Act because the act of paroling the inmate deprived the daughter of her life and liberty. The trial court sustained respondents' demurrer and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and held that both discretionary decisions, such as paroling the inmate, and their ministerial implementation, such as the supervising the parolee, fell under the blanket of immunity provided by Cal. Gov't Code. § 845.8. The court found that respondent employees were acting within their official capacity and were immune from suit under the Civil Rights Act and that § 845.8 was constitutional because there was a rational relationship between the state's purposes and the statute. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sustaining the demurrer without leave to amend because the facts were undisputed, the nature of the claim was clear, but there was no liability under substantive law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, sustaining respondent state and its employees' demurrer, and held that the actions of respondents in paroling the inmate that killed the daughter of appellant father were within their official capacity and covered by governmental immunity. Furthermore, the court held that there was no liability under the Civil Rights Act, and that the statute conferring governmental immunity was constitutional.

 

1853 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Weltsch


Crim. No. 16973


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


84 Cal. App. 3d 959; 149 Cal. Rptr. 112; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1936



September 19, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of the defendant and appellant for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 15, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. C 6878, Alan W. Haverty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order dismissing the information insofar as it charged attempted grand theft is reversed. The purported appeal of the People from certain nonappealable rulings, i.e., "The amendment of the information, on the court's motion and over the objection of the People, to charge violation of California Penal Code Section 351a, a misdemeanor, and the court's action in allowing the defendant to plead guilty to said amended information," is dismissed. (See Pen. Code, § 1238; 6 Witkin, Cal. Procedure (2d ed. 1971) Appeal, § 31, p. 4046.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), dismissing the information charging defendant with attempted grand theft. The state contended that defendant attempted, by false pretenses, to defraud undercover officers of money with intent to commit grand theft as defined by Cal. Penal Code §§ 484 and 487.


OVERVIEW: The people charged defendant by information with the crime of attempted grand theft. The people's theory at defendant's preliminary hearing was that he attempted by false pretenses to defraud certain undercover police officers of money in excess of $ 200. Defendant tried to sell phony bottles of expensive perfume; the bottles' imitation contents were of little or no value. The lower court granted defendant's motion, over the people's objection, to amend the information to charge a misdemeanor; the people appealed the lower court's order. The court held that defendant was properly charged with the felony offense. Defendant cross-appealed, contending that the evidence upon which his misdemeanor plea and conviction were founded was unconstitutionally seized by the officers. The court held that the officers, from the information known to them at the time, had probable cause to seize the bottled substances produced by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the information insofar as it charged attempted grand theft, finding that defendant was properly charged with the felony offense. The court also found that the officers had probable cause to seize the bottled substances produced by defendant.

 

1854 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re David E.


Civ. No. 16876


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


85 Cal. App. 3d 632; 150 Cal. Rptr. 790; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 2009



September 19, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 15, 1978. Mosk, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 389925, Daniel C. Leedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which declared his two minor children free from his custody and control under Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(7) (1977).


OVERVIEW: Appellant father's children were declared free from his custody and control under Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(7) (1977) after the children were placed in foster homes and declared dependent children of the juvenile court. Appellant challenged the trial court's decision on the grounds that § 232(a)(7) was unconstitutional because it only required a showing of clear and convincing evidence that a parent was unable to care for the child, there was insufficient evidence to support the trial court's findings, and because the trial court denied him a jury trial. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and held that there were no constitutional barriers to using the burden of clear and convincing evidence in determining whether appellant's children should be free of their father's control because appellant's liberty was not threatened. Furthermore, the court found that the trial court's findings under § 232(a)(7) were supported by substantial evidence and that appellant was not entitled to a jury trial because a freedom from custody proceeding did not exist at common law and there was no statute providing for a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision declaring appellant father's children free from his custody and control because the findings of the trial court were supported by substantial evidence, the burden of clear and convincing evidence was constitutional, and appellant was not entitled to a jury trial.

 

1855 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Ballard v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 42741


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


84 Cal. App. 3d 885; 149 Cal. Rptr. 82; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1930



September 18, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 15, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 215655, Alan W. Haverty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), that rejected his writ for mandate to compel respondent municipal court to vacate defendant's prior conviction for misdemeanor drunk driving under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102, subd. (a).


OVERVIEW: The court rejected criminal defendant's claim that his petition for writ of mandate to compel respondent municipal court to vacate his prior conviction for misdemeanor drunk driving under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102, subd. (a), should have been granted. Defendant had argued that his prior conviction was unconstitutional because prior to accepting his guilty plea, respondent had not made an inquiry as to the factual basis for the plea, and thus there was not a valid or intelligent waiver by defendant of his rights. Further, defendant argued that the absence of a factual determination requirement constituted a deprivation of equal protection and due process rights under the state constitution, Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, subd. (a), and the federal constitution, U.S. Const. amend XIV. The court held that the legislature had classified the offense as a misdemeanor, which did not require a factual determination by respondent, and such classification was constitutionally permissible because it was made for a lawful state purpose and bore a rational relationship to that purpose. Therefore, the denial of defendant's petition for writ of mandate was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of criminal defendant's petition for writ for mandate to compel respondent municipal court to vacate defendant's prior conviction for misdemeanor drunk driving, holding that a factual inquiry into the basis for defendant's guilty plea was not required in misdemeanor cases, and misdemeanor classification by legislature was not a violation of defendant's due process or equal protection rights.

 

1856 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Willis


Crim. No. 3296


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


84 Cal. App. 3d 952; 149 Cal. Rptr. 301; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1935



September 18, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 15, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 214510-0, Leonard Irving Meyers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of his conviction of robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211 by the Superior Court of Fresno County (California).


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was convicted of several counts of robbery, Cal. Penal Code § 211, which were committed prior to July 1, 1977. Appellant was sentenced under the retroactivity portions of the Uniform Determinate Sentencing Act of 1976, Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2, which provided inmates who commit crimes after July 1, 1977 an opportunity to receive the lower of three prison terms by showing the existence of mitigating factors, but inmates who committed crimes prior to July 1, 1977 were not afforded the same opportunity. Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentencing, and the court affirmed and held that Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2 did not violate appellant's equal protection rights, that appellant's claim that delays in bringing him to trial violated his speedy trial right was without merit, and that appellant failed to show any prejudice from the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentencing and held that appellant's sentencing under the Uniform Determinate Sentencing Act was not a violation of his equal protection rights, and that appellant failed to show that any delay in bringing him to trial violated his right to a speedy trial or prejudiced him in any way.

 

1857 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Gruzen v. Henry


Civ. No 53533


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


84 Cal. App. 3d 515; 148 Cal. Rptr. 573; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1893



September 1, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied September 20, 1978, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied October 25, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the Pasadena Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. CO-56064-C, Gary Klausner, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified by deleting the provision for a money judgment against defendants; otherwise it is affirmed. Neither party shall recover costs in this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant illegal tenants appealed from a Municipal Court for the Pasadena Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California) judgment for plaintiff landlord in his action for unlawful detainer; defendants argued that the rental agreement was void under Pasadena, Cal., Ordinance No. 5121.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord filed an action for unlawful detainer against defendant illegal tenants, attempting to enforce both defendants' eviction and plaintiff's charging of back rent owed. After a judgment in favor of plaintiff, defendants appealed based on their contention that their rental agreement had been void because of plaintiff's failure to secure the certificate of occupancy required by Pasadena, Cal., Ordinance No. 5121. The court found that the ordinance in question was constitutional. Because the lease was invalid under the ordinance, plaintiff could not recover for back rent, although he could legally evict defendants. Finally, a minor defect in the notice to defendants did not require that the judgment against defendants be reversed. Thus, the court modified the judgment and affirmed as modified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with modification, holding that defendants were correct that plaintiff's failure to secure a certificate of occupancy required by a constitutional local ordinance meant that the lease was invalid and that plaintiff could not recover back rent from defendants.

 

1858 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Van Atta v. Scott


Civ. No. 40998.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


84 Cal. App. 3d 450; 148 Cal. Rptr. 717; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1887



Aug. 31, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Nov. 9, 1978 (see 27 C.3d 424)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 662928, Joseph G. Kennedy, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers and defendant police challenged the order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in a taxpayers' action in which they sought to enjoin defendants from expending public funds in the operation of the money bail and "own recognizance" release systems which found that certain aspects of the system violated due process.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers brought a taxpayers' action against defendant police and sought to enjoin them from expending public funds in the operation of money bail and "own recognizance" release systems as they existed in the county. The trial court upheld some aspects of the bail and release programs but determined that the existing system of pretrial detention violated procedural due process. Both parties challenged this decision. This court reversed with directions to dismiss the action because resort to a taxpayers' action under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 526a was unnecessary in a matter such as this where a ready hearing was available to a person directly affected by the challenged practice. The purpose of § 526a was to permit adjudication of challenges against governmental action that might otherwise never have been heard for lack of a party with standing to sue as a plaintiff. In this action any accused person who did not obtain release on bail or on his own recognizance had standing to challenge the alleged due process and equal protection violations suffered under the money bail and "own recognizance" release systems.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order in this taxpayers' action with directions to dismiss because resort to such an action was impermissible as any accused person who did not obtain release on bail or on his own recognizance had standing to sue.

 

1859 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Solorzano


Crim. No. 30577


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


84 Cal. App. 3d 413; 148 Cal. Rptr. 696; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1883



August 30, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied October 25, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A440791, William E. McGinley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed as to count 1 and reversed as to count 2. The superior court is ordered to correct its records to reflect a credit of 36 days pursuant to section 2900.5 of the Penal Code.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), convicting him of violations of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11352(a) and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351, involving more than one-half ounce of a substance containing heroin.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violations of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11352(a) and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351, involving sale or possession of more than one-half ounce of a substance containing heroin, and sentenced under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.07(a)(2). Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed the conviction under § 11352 but reversed the conviction under § 11351, finding that it was a lesser included offense of § 11352(a). The court found that § 1203.07 was constitutional when evaluated under the strict scrutiny test, because the state clearly had a compelling interest in preventing trafficking in the type of substance containing heroin that passed from pusher to addict in the ordinary course of events.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed one count of defendant's conviction for sale of one-half ounce or more of a substance containing heroin and reversed the second count as a lesser included offense. The court ordered the trial court to reflect a credit of 36 days rather than 26 days.

 

1860 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Umansky v. Urquhart


Civ. No. 16050


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


84 Cal. App. 3d 368; 148 Cal. Rptr. 547; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1874



August 29, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 375502, Daniel C. Leedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor sought review from a Superior Court of San Diego County (California) judgment for defendant attorneys in plaintiff's suit against them, which alleged abuse of process in the filing of a punitive damages claim that did not lie under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 377.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff doctor was sued by decedent's heirs for wrongful death. After an amended complaint was filed deleting a punitive damages cause of action, plaintiff sued defendant attorneys for abuse of process, alleging that defendants had filed suit although the punitive damages cause did not lie under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 377. When the lower court entered judgment for defendants, plaintiff sought review. The court held that although § 377 did limit recovery of heirs suing for punitive damages, the privilege granted by Cal. Civ. Code § 47(2) was intended to allow free access to the courts in order to allow, among other things, for the testing of the validity of statutes. Thus, where the constitutionality of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 377 had not been determined in practical application it was proper for the privilege to attach and for the judgment to be affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that although the statute invoked by plaintiff doctor did prohibit recovery of punitive damages in the case, the constitutionality of that prohibition had not been tested in the appellate courts and there was no reason not to attach the privilege protecting defendant attorneys from plaintiff's claim.

 

1861 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County


Civ. No. 53175.Civ. No. 53234.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


84 Cal. App. 3d 267; 148 Cal. Rptr. 513; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1863



August 24, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] as modified Sept. 7, 1978.
Hg. den. Oct. 18, 1978, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; Rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner people and petitioner public guardian each sought a writ of mandate to direct respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to vacate its orders initiating conservatorship proceedings upon findings that real party defendant was gravely disabled within the meaning of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5008(h).


OVERVIEW: Real party defendant had a 25 count felony indictment pending against him. He was found to be competent to stand trial by a jury, but respondent trial court entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict finding him mentally incompetent to stand trial. Subsequently, upon hospital superintendent's withdrawal of his prior certification of competency made pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1372, respondent found that real party was gravely disabled within the meaning of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5008(h) and ordered the county public guardian to initiate conservatorship proceedings. Petitioner people filed a motion to vacate the order, which was denied. Thereafter, petitioner people and petitioner public guardian sought a writ of mandate. The court issued the writ to vacate respondent's orders, finding that respondent's conduct with respect to the superintendent's certification of competence was wholly inappropriate, and that the appropriate course of action would be for criminal proceedings to resume pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1372 based upon the superintendent's certification. The court also found that respondent's order initiating conservatorship proceedings premature.


OUTCOME: A writ of mandate was issued directing respondent trial court to vacate its orders initiating conservatorship proceedings after finding that real party defendant was gravely disabled because respondent's conduct with respect to the superintendent's certification of real party's competence was inappropriate and the initiation of conservatorship proceedings was premature.

 

1862 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


North Los Angeles County Regional Center v. Jarakian


Civ. No. 19769


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


84 Cal. App. 3d 157; 148 Cal. Rptr. 296; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1848



August 22, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On September 19, 1978, the opinion was modified to read as printed above.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. 178843, Charles Bierschbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the case is remanded to the superior court for further proceedings according to appellant all the rights accorded all other developmentally disabled persons.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developmentally disabled person sought review of the order of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which committed him to respondent state department of health for suitable care and treatment pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6514.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developmentally disabled person was a voluntary resident at a state hospital. He was committed involuntarily to respondent state department of health pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6514 based on findings that he was not capable of providing for his basic needs for food, clothing, and shelter, that he was not able to protect himself from ordinary threats to life, health, or safety, and that he was not willing to accept suitable treatment on a voluntary basis. Appellant challenged the commitment order on the basis that voluntary or nonprotesting state hospital patients were subject to a less exacting standard than other developmentally disabled persons insofar as the commitment of any other developmentally disabled patient required a finding that the patient was a danger to himself or others. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that there was no discernible state interest upon which to justify the statutory distinction between developmentally disabled persons who are voluntary residents of a state hospital and all other developmentally disabled persons. The cause was remanded to afford appellant a hearing on dangerousness before commitment.


OUTCOME: The order committing appellant developmentally disabled person to respondent state department of health for treatment was reversed. There was no compelling state interest that justified disparate treatment of voluntary residents of state hospitals and all other developmentally disabled persons. Therefore, appellant was entitled to a hearing on whether he posed a danger to himself or others before being involuntarily committed.

 

1863 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Perez


Crim. No. 9922


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


84 Cal. App. 3d 168; 148 Cal. Rptr. 302; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1849



August 22, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons heretofore stated the writ is granted, the return to the order to show cause shall stand as the return to the writ, and the sentence entered on June 2, 1977, is set aside, and petitioner is ordered to appear in the municipal court to be arraigned for pronouncement of judgment. Upon such arraignment the municipal court will have power to consider, and discretion to grant or deny, an application for probation, if petitioner so requests, and will have the power and the duty to pronounce judgment for the offense of which petitioner stands convicted but, by reason of this order, not sentenced.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought habeas corpus, and the California supreme court returned the matter to the court. Petitioner was convicted of misdemeanor drunk driving, Cal. Veh. Code § 23102, after a jury trial in a municipal court. Petitioner complained that the municipal court improperly augmented his punishment because it believed that he committed and suborned perjury.


OVERVIEW: After conviction of misdemeanor drunk driving, Cal. Veh. Code § 23101, petitioner sought habeas corpus, which the California Supreme Court sent back to the court. The court summarily rejected petitioner's claim that the municipal court gave him a greater punishment, 120 days in jail, a $ 500 fine, and six-month suspension of driving license and privileges, because he demanded a jury trial. The court, however, granted the writ because of petitioner's claim that the municipal court augmented his punishment because of the belief he both committed and suborned perjury. The court explained because the consideration of perjury in the appraisal of a defendant's character ran the risk of being improperly expanded to support the imposition of punishment for the perjury itself, rather than going to amenability to rehabilitation, the trial judge who injected the subject into the sentencing process should have expressly stated that its consideration was not to punish the perjury, which would have violated due process. The court rejected plaintiff's argument of cruel and unusual punishment as bordering on the frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus and set aside his sentencing in the municipal court for misdemeanor drunk driving because of the possibility the sentence included a punishment for perjury. The court explained that the municipal court would have had the power to consider, and the discretion to grant or deny, an application for probation, rather than the jail sentence previously imposed.

 

1864 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Cervantez v. J. C. Penney Co.


Civ. No. 15614.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


84 Cal. App. 3d 96; 148 Cal. Rptr. 467; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1843



August 21, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Oct. 18, 1978 (see 24 C.3d 579)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 192640, Walter E. Smith, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment for defendants from the Superior Court of Orange County (California) in his action to recover damages for personal injuries allegedly sustained as a result of his arrest.


OVERVIEW: After observing criminal activity, defendant peace officer, while working part-time as a security officer for defendant store, detained plaintiff. In plaintiff's subsequent suit against defendant store and defendant peace officer, the trial court granted defendants' motion for nonsuit as to the causes of action for intentional infliction of emotional distress and negligence and a trial resulted in a jury verdict for defendants on the remaining causes of action. Plaintiff appealed, contending that the trial court erred in holding that defendant peace officer was acting as a peace officer at the time of the arrest. The court affirmed the decision, holding that defendant retained his status of peace officer for purposes of determining the lawfulness of the arrest pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 836. Neither the circumstance that defendant was off duty nor the fact that he was working as a security guard affected his status as a peace officer where he had territorial jurisdiction pursuant to an agreement between municipal police departments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that defendant peace officer's off-duty status and the fact that he was working as a security guard for defendant store did not affect his status as a peace officer because he had territorial jurisdiction pursuant to a consent agreement executed by municipal police departments.

 

1865 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Terry D.


Civ. No. 16071


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


83 Cal. App. 3d 890; 148 Cal. Rptr. 221; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1821



August 16, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Butte County, Nos. AB 1334, 1335, 1336, 1337, 1338 and 1339, Reginald M. Watt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter is remanded to the superior court for the single purpose of reconsideration of findings numbers 9 and 10 in light of this opinion, applying the standard of clear and convincing evidence to the facts as developed in the previous hearings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which entered judgment in favor of respondent Butte County Department of Social Welfare (California), declaring appellant's six minor children free from parental custody and control pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(2), (7).


OVERVIEW: After a long history of neglect and poor record of parental visitation while appellant's minor children were in foster care, respondent Butte County Department of Social Welfare (California) petitioned to have appellant's minor children declared free from parental custody and control pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(2), (7). The trial court granted the petitions. The court reversed the judgment, and remanded the cause for the sole purpose of applying the standard of clear and convincing evidence as to certain factual findings of neglect under § 232(a)(2). The court rejected appellant's remaining contentions. The distinctions in burdens of proof for termination of parental rights provided by § 232(a)(2) and § 232(a)(7) were justified by the state's compelling interest in promotion of child welfare, even though a rational basis for the distinction would have sufficed due to the absence of a suspect classification. The court rejected appellant's contention that evaluation of parental conduct should be restricted to the two-year foster home period, and held that a parent's conduct prior to that period could be considered in evaluating parents' ability to care for their children.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the cause remanded only for the purpose of considering certain factual determinations of parental neglect under the clear and convincing evidence standard. The trial court had erroneously applied the preponderance of evidence test to the question of parental neglect. However, there was no constitutional defect in the statutory tests for determining whether parental rights should be terminated.

 

1866 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Credit Ins. Gen. Agents Assn. v. Payne


Civ. No. 52741


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


83 Cal. App. 3d 870; 148 Cal. Rptr. 141; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1819



August 16, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 59937, Robert I. Weil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied its motion for a new trial or to vacate the judgment in favor of respondent commissioner in appellant's suit to restrain enforcement of Cal. Code Reg. tit. 10, §§ 2248.1- 2248.25 and to declare that respondent lacked statutory authority to restrict the maximum amount of compensation paid to insurer's general agents.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer had sued for declaratory and injunctive relief, seeking to restrain enforcement of Cal. Code Reg. tit. 10, §§ 2248.1- 2248.25 as well as a declaration that respondent commission was without statutory authority to restrict the maximum compensation due to general agents of insurers in the credit insurance industry in California. The trial court entered judgment in favor of respondent and then denied appellant's motion for a new trial or to vacate the judgment. On appeal, the court determined that the result reached by respondent, which was the regulation of compensation of insurer's general agents, was not arbitrary, capricious, or entirely lacking in evidentiary support. The court noted that the regulation was designed to see that benefits provided to insureds were reasonable in relation to premiums charged. The court affirmed, finding that respondent possessed the power to limit commissions payable to agents within his statutory control and that no constitutional rights had been infringed by the statutes in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent commissioner, finding that appellant insurer was properly denied his motion for a new trial or to vacate the judgment where respondent had the power, pursuant to valid statutory authority, to restrict the compensation due to general agents of credit insurers because the statutes in question were not arbitrary or capricious and did not infringe appellant's constitutional rights.

 

1867 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Eden v. Van Tine


Civ. No. 47185


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


83 Cal. App. 3d 879; 148 Cal. Rptr. 215; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1820; 12 A.L.R.4th 856



August 16, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 57037, August J. Goebel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of dismissal of plaintiffs' cause of action against Van Tine and Maro, and the judgment of dismissal of Van Tine's cross-complaint against Maro, are all reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment of dismissal against them in their action against defendant builders, ruling that the causes of action were barred by the statute of limitations contained in sections Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §§ 337.1(a), 337.15(a).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff home buyers filed an action against defendant builders seeking damages based on negligence and strict liability in the construction of property they bought. After purchasing the property, plaintiffs discovered that a section of patio wall had fallen. Plaintiffs determined that the land was unstable and that the residence had suffered substantial structural distress requiring considerable reconstruction. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' action as time-barred by Cal. Civ. Code §§ 337.1(a), 337.15(a). The court reversed, holding that if retroactive application of the statute of limitations deprived plaintiffs of a reasonable opportunity to exercise their remedy, retroactive application was unconstitutional as to plaintiffs. When plaintiffs discovered the latent defect, operation of the statute of limitations would have reduced the time they had to bring an action to two months and five days. Under prior law, they would have had three years after notice of the latent defect to commence a cause of action. Therefore, § 337.15 reduced their period to file to a reasonable time after the discovery of the defect, which plaintiffs had met by filing within five months.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of plaintiff's action against defendant builders and the concomitant dismissal of defendant builders' cross-complaint against cross-defendant builders were reversed, and the causes remanded for trial. Retroactive application of the statute of limitations had deprived plaintiffs of a reasonable time within which to bring an action after discovering a latent defect. Plaintiffs' filing five months after the discovery was thus timely.

 

1868 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bartman v. Estate of Bartman


Civ. No. 43083


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


83 Cal. App. 3d 780; 148 Cal. Rptr. 207; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1810



August 14, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied October 25, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sonoma County, No. 88755, Joseph P. Murphy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant decedent's daughter sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California), which dismissed the negligence action that appellant brought against respondent decedent's estate pursuant to Cal. Prob. Code § 721, on the ground that appellant had not filed a creditor's claim against respondent within the time limits set by Cal. Prob. Code § 700 et seq.


OVERVIEW: At the time of an automobile accident in which decedent was killed and appellant decedent's daughter was injured, Cal. Veh. Code § 17158 deprived an injured automobile guest of recovery for the careless driving of his host. After § 17158 was declared unconstitutional and after the period in which appellant could file a creditor's claim against respondent decedent's estate expired under Cal. Prob. Code § 707, appellant brought an action pursuant to Cal. Prob. Code § 721, for damages resulting from decedent's negligence. The trial court dismissed appellant's § 721 claim on the ground that appellant did not timely file a creditor's claim. The court affirmed the dismissal because appellant could not invoke the benefit of § 721, which provided for an independent action against an estate up to the limits of a decedent's liability insurance, and because § 721 did not have retroactive application. The court held that appellant's claim was not revived by the retroactive application of case law declaring the automobile guest statute unconstitutional because the claim for personal injuries was barred by the statute of limitations set forth in Cal. Prob. Code § 700 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant decedent's daughter's action for personal injuries against respondent decedent's estate where the action was barred by the statute of limitations governing creditors' claims. The court held that appellant's barred claim was not revived by the retrospective application of subsequent law and that a statute providing for the filing of independent actions against estates was not retroactive.

 

1869 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Guardianship of Tulley


Civ. No. 42514


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


83 Cal. App. 3d 698; 146 Cal. Rptr. 266; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1802



August 10, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied October 4, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 55171, Gerald E. Ragan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian challenged an order of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) denying his request to order the sterilization of his natural daughter and ward, contending that due to her incapacity she was unable to comprehend her personal needs or to cope with her menstrual cycle, and that it would be in her best interest that she be surgically sterilized.


OVERVIEW: Appellant guardian sought review of an order which denied his request to allow the sterilization of his natural daughter, who had the mental facilities of a three year old. The lower court denied his request on the ground that it was not authorized to approve involuntary sterilization. On appeal, the court examined the controlling statute, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 7254, and held that the statutory requirements included institutionalization of the individual. Additionally, the court held that because the California Legislature had enacted a statutory scheme, and sterilization was a very serious and irreversible procedure, common law foundations for the authority to compel sterilization were insufficient safeguard's of an individual's rights. Finally, the court held that any action by the court in contravention of the controlling statute would amount to an unacceptable judicial encroachment on the province of the legislature, and the court affirmed the lower court's order denying appellant's request.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant guardian's request to have his natural daughter and ward sterilized, holding that because sterilization amounted to a serious invasion of one's body, the procedural safeguards under the controlling statutes, including institutionalization, had to be met prior to the judiciary's authorization to sterilize an individual.

 

1870 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cramblit


Crim. No. 9216


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


84 Cal. App. 3d 437; 148 Cal. Rptr. 440; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1886



July 31, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied September 27, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 47988, Fred W. Marler, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants junk metal dealers sought review of jury convictions from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), challenging misdemeanor sentences, reduced to probation, for violating Cal. Penal Code § 496a, which criminalized the failure of junk dealers to use due diligence to ascertain the authority of persons seeking to sell metal parts of the sort ordinarily used by public utilities.


OVERVIEW: Defendant junk metal dealers challenged the jury's verdict convicting them of buying water meters from a plainclothes police officer without using due diligence to determine whether the officer had authority to sell meters that belonged to a public utility, an offense criminalized under Cal. Penal Code § 496a. Defendants bought the meters as scrap metal without ascertaining the seller's identity or authority to sell the meters.
