Kilpatrick's Bakeries, Inc. v. Unemployment Ins. Appeals Bd.


Civ. No. 39459


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


77 Cal. App. 3d 539; 143 Cal. Rptr. 664; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1238



February 10, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of the defendants and respondents for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied May 11, 1978. Bird, C. J., Tobriner, J., and Mosk, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 4666501, George W. Phillips, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employers sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which upheld the decision of respondent California Unemployment Insurance Appeals Board granting benefits to union employees who became unemployed as a result of a labor dispute.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellant employers' petition for a writ of mandamus and upheld the decision of respondent California Unemployment Insurance Appeals Board granting benefits to union employees who became unemployed as a result of a labor dispute. Appellants sought review and a writ of mandate that their unemployment insurance reserve account be relieved of all charges. The court held that the trial court should have independently reviewed respondent's decision instead of applying the substantial evidence test. The court found that appellants had a fundamental vested property right which was substantially affected by the award of unemployment insurance benefits, and that the independent judgment test applied both to employee appeals and employer appeals. The court reversed and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded because the trial court should have independently reviewed the decision of respondent California Unemployment Insurance Appeals Board when appellant employer sought review, rather than applying the substantial evidence test.

 

1937 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


Crim. No. 30512


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


77 Cal. App. 3d 455; 143 Cal. Rptr. 587; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1229; 3 A.L.R.4th 1185



February 8, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 326801, Richard F. C. Hayden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: As modified the judgment (order granting probation) is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that convicted appellant of four counts of pimping in violation of Cal Penal Code § 266h and sentenced defendant to probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of pimping in violation of Cal. Penal Code §266h. All four counts involved the same prostitute; they differed only as to the dates of the alleged offense. On appeal, the court modified the trial court's judgment. The court held that living or deriving support or maintenance from the earnings of a prostitute knowing her to be a prostitute was an ongoing continuing offense that occurred over a period of time. The court held that defendant was guilty of only one count of pimping because there was only one continuous course of conduct involving one prostitute even though it occurred over a long period of time. The court affirmed the condition of probation imposed on defendant that provided defendant was not to work in bars, taxicabs, or other locations suitable for acting as a pimp. The court held that the condition served the statutory ends of probation and was valid because it bore a relationship to the crime of pimping since bars and taxicabs are ideal locations for conducting pimping activities. The court also held that the phrase "other locations suitable for acting as a pimp" prevented the condition from being unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of four counts of pimping. The judgment was modified to convict defendant of only one count of pimping because the record established only one continuing criminal act. The court affirmed the conditions of probation imposed on defendant because they served the statutory ends of probation and were not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1938 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Blue Star Line, Inc. v. City and County of San Francisco


Civ. No. 39195


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


77 Cal. App. 3d 429; 143 Cal. Rptr. 647; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1227



February 8, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied March 3, 1978, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Nos. 645950, 649827, Joseph G. Kennedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, steamship lines, steamship agents, and stevedore firms, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) entered in favor of respondent city in appellants' declaratory judgment action that asserted that a payroll tax imposed by respondent was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city imposed a payroll tax upon the payrolls of employers who conducted business within its territorial limits. Appellants, steamship lines, steamship agents, and stevedore firms, filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the tax. Appellants were engaged in international maritime commerce. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found that the tax was constitutional. The court found that no international treaties prohibited the tax. The court held that the import-export clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2 did not prohibit the tax because the tax reached only the dockside handling of imported and exported goods by appellants' employees; the tax did not reach the goods themselves. The court held that the tax was not prohibited by the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, because the tax reached a taxable nexus, it was fairly apportioned to a local activity, it did not discriminate against employees engaged in foreign commerce since it was imposed on all employers in the city, and it was fairly related to the services provided by respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that found respondent city's payroll tax that was imposed on appellants, steamship lines, steamship agents, and stevedore firms, was constitutional. The tax did not violate any treaties and was not prohibited by the import-export clause or the commerce clauses of the United States Constitution.

 

1939 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Kelvin M.


Civ. No. 41182


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


77 Cal. App. 3d 396; 143 Cal. Rptr. 561; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1223



February 6, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 103830, Carl W. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Since the juvenile court erred in making the jurisdictional order of December 10, it was without jurisdiction to make the dispositional order of December 13. We therefore reverse both orders.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which sustained a petition that declared a minor a dependent of the juvenile court pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 600(a).


OVERVIEW: At a jurisdictional hearing, appellant father objected to the juvenile court's jurisdiction over a minor. Appellant made an offer of proof that as the natural father, he was willing and capable of exercising control over the minor. The juvenile court held that appellant's offer of proof was irrelevant, and sustained a petition that declared the minor a dependent of the juvenile court. On appeal, the court held that appellant's notice of appeal was timely filed. Next, the court considered the merits of the appeal. The court held that the juvenile court's ruling pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 600(a) denied appellant due process of law because appellant was not afforded adequate notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court held that the juvenile court erred in making its jurisdictional order because appellant was not allowed to present evidence that showed his willingness and ability to control and care for the minor. The court reversed the juvenile court's jurisdictional and dispositional order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the juvenile court's order that declared the minor a dependent of the juvenile court because appellant father's due process rights were violated, as he was not afforded adequate notice and an opportunity to be heard.

 

1940 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Robertson v. Willis


Civ. No. 51134


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


77 Cal. App. 3d 358; 143 Cal. Rptr. 523; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1220



February 2, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied February 21, 1978. Jefferson (Bernard), J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted. Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied May 1, 1978. Bird, C. J., Mosk, J., and Manuel, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NW C 21442, Milton L. Most, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified by adding thereto the following provision: "It Is Further Ordered, Adjudged And Decreed that the liability of defendant Frances Willis is limited to the extent of her interest in the community property owned by her and John Willis." As thus modified, the judgment is affirmed. Respondent shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a personal judgment against her in plaintiff's suit brought on a debt incurred by defendant's husband. Defendant did not dispute that community property was subject to that debt, but appealed the entry of a personal judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's husband incurred a business debt to plaintiff. The practice of husband and wife had been to keep their earnings segregated with each spouse paying certain bills. After the husband's death, plaintiff sued defendant wife for the debt. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the holding that defendant's interest in the community property was subject to the debt owed to plaintiff, but the court said that this did not warrant entry of a judgment against defendant wife personally. The court said that the retroactive effect of 1975 amendments to Cal. Civ. Code § 5116 was not unconstitutional. That statute, as amended, provided that the community was liable for contracts of either spouse made before or after January 1, 1975. Previously the law had provided that the wife's earnings were not liable for the husband's debts. The court said that plaintiff was not entitled to a personal judgment against defendant wife because plaintiff had not shown that defendant wife was unjustly enriched or that the net value of the community estate had been diminished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the community property of defendant wife and her husband, including property accumulated from defendant's earnings, was liable for payment of defendant's husband's debt to plaintiff. The court modified the judgment to clarify that defendant was not personally liable for the debt although her interest in the community property was.

 

1941 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Civil Service Com.


Civ. No. 16302


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


77 Cal. App. 3d 234; 143 Cal. Rptr. 483; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1207; 21 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1506; 16 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8158



Jan. 30, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted May 18, 1978 (See 26 C.3d 257)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county civil service commission (commission) and board of supervisors, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted a peremptory writ against defendants and held that defendant commission's rule and order unconstitutionally discriminated against nonminorities, in plaintiff district attorney's action to challenge the implementation of a rule that established a minority quota hiring system.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff district attorney filed a mandate petition in the trial court against defendants, county civil service commission (commission) and board of supervisors, seeking abrogation of defendant commission's rule and order, which established a minority quota hiring system whenever necessary to remedy an imbalance in county agencies. The trial court granted the peremptory writ, and the court affirmed. The court held that defendant commission's minority preference order violated the Sacramento County Charter and exceeded the authority granted by Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 (Title VII). The order injected racial, ethnic, and gender qualifications into a hiring system whose charter commanded disregard of race, ethnicity, and gender. The order violated the competitive qualification and anti-discrimination provisions of the charter. The action of defendant commission overstepped the objective of Title VII, which was the removal of artificial, arbitrary, and unnecessary barriers to employment when the barriers operated invidiously to discriminate on the basis of racial or other impermissible classifications, and established a barrier to the employment of majority applicants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which abrogated defendant county civil service commission's (commission) rule regarding minority applicants. Defendant commission's order establishing a minority quota hiring system overstepped Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964's objectives and created a barrier to employment of majority applicants, which violated the charter's competitive qualification and anti-discrimination provisions.

 

1942 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Agricultural Labor Relations Board v. Super Court of Riverside County


Civ. No. 19156


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION Two


77 Cal. App. 3d 248; 143 Cal. Rptr. 633; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1208



January 30, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Hg. den. Apr. 27, 1978, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14, Rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Agricultural Labor Relations Board (ALRB) sought a writ of mandate to require respondent Superior Court of Riverside County (California), to issue orders to real parties in interest employers compelling obedience to administrative subpoenas duces tecum issued by ALRB, requiring production of a "pre-petition employee list" of names, current street addresses, and job classifications of all agricultural employees.


OVERVIEW: A union gave notice of intent to organize the agricultural employees of real party employers who provided a "pre-petition employee list." Petitioner Agricultural Labor Relations Board deemed the list inadequate for lack of current street addresses and, pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 1151(a), issued subpoenas duces tecum to real parties for employee lists as described in Cal. Admin. Code tit. 8, § 20310(a)(2). The trial court ordered real parties orders to show cause why enforcement orders should not issue. The real parties filed declarations establishing that they had furnished to petitioner all the information obtainable about their employees. The trial court found the employee lists set forth the current street addresses to the extent such existed and were obtainable and were not deficient. The trial court ruled that real parties had complied with the subpoenas and, therefore, denied petitioner's applications for enforcement orders. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying petitioner's applications for enforcement orders, and that the trial court's determination that real parties complied with the subpoenas was dispositive.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for writ of mandate, concluding that the trial court's determination that the real parties in interest employers had complied with the subpoenas, in that they had furnished petitioner Agricultural Labor Relations Board all the employee information obtainable and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying petitioner's applications for enforcement orders.

 

1943 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Lemelle v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 19109


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


77 Cal. App. 3d 148; 143 Cal. Rptr. 450; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1199



January 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's application for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 13, 1978. Bird, C. J., Tobriner, J., and Mosk, J., were of the opinion that the application should be granted.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied. The alternative writ heretofore issued is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of respondent Orange County Superior Court (California), which denied his discovery request to real party in interest state for any medical, psychiatric, or psychological records pertaining to defendant's arresting officers as well as crime or arrest reports involving specific offenses which the officers had filed in the preceding 10 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, charged with drug and resisting arrest offenses, sought from real party in interest state discovery of records of the arresting officers' medical, psychiatric, or psychological treatment containing opinions on the officers' character trait for acts of aggression, violence, excessive force, or demonstrating racial or ethnic bias or prejudice. Defendant also sought all crime or arrest reports filed by either officer within the last 10 years involving resisting arrest or battery on a police officer. The lower court denied the request and the appellate court affirmed. Defendant supplied the court with a record insufficient to permit an evaluation of the lower court's exercise of discretion. Further, it was not an abuse of discretion to deny defendant's request for the officers' medical and psychiatric records because they were privileged under Cal. Evid. Code §§ 300, 910, 1010-1026. Moreover, the exception of Cal. Evid. Code § 1024 did not apply because defendant failed to raise it below and there was no factual support for its application. Finally, defendant was due no response on the arrest and crime report request because to do so would have been unduly burdensome.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's discovery request and refused his petition for a writ of mandate to respondent superior court because defendant supplied the appellate court with an inadequate record for review and the information defendant sought to have discovered was either privileged or unduly burdensome to supply.

 

1944 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bosco v. Justice Court


Civ. No. 3377


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


77 Cal. App. 3d 179; 143 Cal. Rptr. 468; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1201



January 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of the plaintiff and appellant for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 23, 1978. Tobriner, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Tulare County, No. 84526, Jay R. Ballantyne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed insofar as it holds section 11550 not to be vague, but is reversed insofar as it holds section 11550 unconstitutional as a violation of the cruel or unusual punishment clause or the equal protection clause.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which held that Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11550 was not unconstitutionally vague. The state also appealed the judgment, which held that § 11550 was unconstitutional because it violated both cruel and unusual punishment and equal protection clauses.


OVERVIEW: Conduct involving controlled substances was prohibited by Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11550, and a mandatory 90-day sentence was given anyone convicted thereunder. Though defendant had not yet gone to trial, the court reviewed her claims using three distinct techniques: (1) the nature of the offense and the offender, with particular regard to the degree of danger each present to society; (2) a comparison of § 11550's punishment with punishments in the state for more serious offenses; and (3) a comparison of § 11550's penalty with punishment in other states for the same offense. Though the court found § 11550 poorly drafted, because the state had discretion either to prosecute or send offenders to diversion programs, the sentence would not be imposed in every case where § 11550 was violated. Given these factors and the fact that § 11550 did not punish a condition of addiction but rather an act, the court found that the mandatory sentence did not impose cruel and unusual punishment. Because it did not punish status, it did not violate the equal protection clause. The acts prohibited by § 11550 met the reasonable certainty test and thus it was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment to the extent that it held the statute was unconstitutional because it violated cruel or unusual punishment or equal protection clauses. The court affirmed the lower court judgment that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1945 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Mountain View Chamber of Commerce v. City of Mountain View


Civ. No. 39724


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


77 Cal. App. 3d 82; 143 Cal. Rptr. 441; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1194



January 25, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified February 2, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 344323, Albert F. DeMarco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, chamber of commerce and sign owners, challenged an order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which denied appellants' request for declaratory and injunctive relief, and sustained respondent city's demurrer without leave to amend on the ground that appellants failed to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, chamber of commerce and sign owners, brought an action to enjoin the enforcement of respondent city's sign regulations and sought declaratory relief claiming that the regulations were unconstitutional as applied to zoning districts in which appellants had located their businesses. The trial court denied the injunction and sustained respondent's demurrer without leave to amend. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellants' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to hear the matter. The court found that appellants had not availed themselves to the variance procedures provided in Mountain View, Cal., Mun. Code § 36.44 and thus failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court determined that no exception to the exhaustion of administrative remedies doctrine had applied because appellants were not irreparably injured by the sign regulations, it would not have been futile for appellants to pursue an administrative remedy, a constitutional challenge required exhaustion of remedies, and appellants' actions had not involved public rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellants', chamber of commerce and sign owners, injunction and sustaining respondent city's demurrer without leave to amend. The court held that appellants' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to hear the case.

 

1946 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Northwestern Mut. Ins. Co. v. Farmers' Ins. Group


Civ. No. 17755


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


76 Cal. App. 3d 1031; 143 Cal. Rptr. 415; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1187



January 23, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 23, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. 152168, Harold R. Haberkorn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: No error appears. The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant primary insurers appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) that was entered in favor of plaintiff excess insurer in a subrogation action to recover from defendants the amount that plaintiff was required to pay on the judgments that were entered against the estate of defendants' insured.


OVERVIEW: A fatal accident occurred involving a vehicle insured by defendant primary insurers. The policy contained an omnibus clause covering permissive users. After defendants refused to settle for less than their policy limits, wrongful death claims were brought against the estate of the permissive user who was alleged to have been the driver. A judgment was entered against the estate. Defendants paid their policy limits on each judgment and plaintiff excess insurer, which had issued a policy to the permissive user, paid the balance. Plaintiff then sued defendants, claiming that their failure to settle was in bad faith. A judgment was entered for plaintiff and defendants appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that the estate would have had a cause of action against defendants, as primary insurers under Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.9, for a bad faith refusal to settle since the proposed settlement was within the policy limits and was presumed reasonable. Thus, plaintiff, as an excess insurer, could recover from defendants, under equitable subrogation, that amount the estate could have recovered since it suffered a loss by being required to pay the balance of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendants had refused to settle within the policy limits, creating a cause of action against them by the insured's permissive user, so that plaintiff was subrogated to the permissive user's rights when it made payments on the judgments that were entered against his estate.

 

1947 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Serna


Crim. No. 30154


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


76 Cal. App. 3d 1010; 143 Cal. Rptr. 350; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1185



January 20, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioners' Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 30, 1978. Newman, J., was of the Opinion that the Application should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County, No. HC-221, Harry E. Woolpert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant superintendent of the California men's colony sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California), which granted habeas corpus relief sought by respondent prisoners at the colony to open an outside bank account.


OVERVIEW: Respondent prisoners filed a petition for writ of "mandamus" which the court treated as a petition for writ of habeas corpus in the trial court alleging that they were being unconstitutionally denied the right to send money to their outside church bank account. The trial court ordered appellant superintendent to allow donations to the bank account in accordance with provisions in the department of correction's rules concerning prisoner contributions to outside charities. On review, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed the trial court to dismiss their petition. The court held that the trial court had erred in granting relief because respondents failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court found that respondents were entitled to appeal the denial of the outside bank account by the superintendent directly to the director of the department and to obtain a ruling within 20 days under the department of corrections' administrative manual. The failure of respondents to exhaust these administrative options foreclosed consideration of their habeas petition by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting habeas corpus relief to respondent prisoners, holding that, because respondents had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies by appealing the issue within the department of corrections prior to filing this action in the superior court, they were not entitled to habeas relief.

 

1948 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gard


Crim. No. 15873


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


76 Cal. App. 3d 998; 143 Cal. Rptr. 346; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1183



January 20, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 10, 1978, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 16, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 18710, Max Wilcox, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physician sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which convicted defendant of conspiracy in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 182, possession for sale of amphetamines and barbiturates in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11378, and transporting and offering to sell amphetamines and barbiturates in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11379.


OVERVIEW: Defendant physician sought reversal of his conviction for conspiracy in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 182, possession for sale of amphetamines and barbiturates in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11378, and transporting and offering to sell amphetamines and barbiturates in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11379. Defendant challenged the state's authority to regulate the distribution of selling controlled substances to other physicians and alleged that the federal Controlled Substances Act, 21 U.S.C.S. § 801 et seq., occupied the field. Defendant also argued that he was not provided with a preliminary hearing. On review, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a preliminary hearing because he had been indicted by a grand jury. The court also found that federal law did not occupy the field of the regulation of controlled substances because state law was not an obstacle to the accomplishment and objectives of the federal statute and because states traditionally were permitted to regulate narcotic traffic within their borders. The court held that federal law had clearly not preempted the field.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction because defendant physician was not entitled to a preliminary hearing as he was indicted by a grand jury and state law regulating the sale and possession of controlled substances was not preempted by federal law.

 

1949 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Battin


Crim. No. 9051


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


77 Cal. App. 3d 635; 143 Cal. Rptr. 731; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1246; 95 A.L.R.3d 248



January 18, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied February 15, 1978, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 13, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. C 34528, Kenneth E. Lae, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which convicted defendant for misuse of public funds in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 424(2), and sentenced him to three years' informal probation on condition that defendant would serve six months in the county jail (with five months suspended), a fine plus penalty assessments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an elected county supervisor, was a candidate for another elective office. During his campaign, he utilized his county-paid supervisor staff workers and county-provided space and equipment for campaign activities. The county-paid staff was utilized for campaign activities during county working hours. On appeal, defendant challenged the application of Cal. Penal Code § 424(2) to his campaign activities, and the constitutionality of § 424(2). Defendant also contended that the state failed to prove that a violation of § 424 occurred, that the jury was not instructed concerning specific intent, that his conviction was not a felony, that the prosecutor failed to subpoena campaign volunteers as witnesses before the grand jury, that the acquittal verdict on charges that he presented fraudulent claims under Cal. Penal Code § 72 was inconsistent with the conviction that he violated, § 424(2), and that he was a victim of discriminatory prosecution. The court affirmed and held that § 424(2) was properly applied to defendant's campaign activities, that there was substantial evidence to support a jury verdict, and that § 424(2) was not vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for misuse of public funds because defendant's use of county-paid workers and equipment for a political campaign constituted misuse of public funds, and that the violation was not a specific intent crime. The court also held that defendant's acquittal on another charge was not inconsistent with his conviction, and that defendant had not shown that he had been subject to discriminatory prosecution.

 

1950 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Keller


Crim. No. 8565


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


76 Cal. App. 3d 827; 143 Cal. Rptr. 184; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1169



January 13, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 31, 1978, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 9, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR-37783, Norbert Ehrenfreund, Earl H. Maas, Jr., and Benjamin W. Hamrick, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) convicting him of possession of heroin. Defendant pleaded guilty after an unsuccessful motion to suppress evidence. The search and discovery of contraband was based on a waiver of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights as a condition of probation for an earlier conviction of petty theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of heroin after the trial court denied his motion to suppress evidence. The search and discovery of the contraband was based on defendant's waiver of his U.S. Const. amend. IV rights required as a condition of probation for an earlier conviction of petty theft. The court reversed the conviction, holding that the waiver was not reasonably related to nor was it a reasonable deterrent to the crime of petty theft. Defendant's probation in the petty theft conviction was based on "narcotics conditions". Although defendant had a history of narcotics use, there was nothing that linked the theft with narcotics activity. After examining the existing case law and finding that restrictions of constitutional rights required special scrutiny, the court held that probation with narcotics conditions was excessive for defendant's earlier conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of heroin possession, holding that the condition of probation that defendant waive his Fourth Amendment rights was not reasonably related to the conviction of the crime of petty theft.

 

1951 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bodle v. Bodle


Civ. No. 14821


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


76 Cal. App. 3d 758; 143 Cal. Rptr. 115; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1164



January 11, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 27, 1978, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 9, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. D-19293, Earl H. Maas, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of an order by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied her order to show cause in a divorce proceeding, in which she claimed one-half of the United States Navy retirement pension being paid to respondent ex-husband.


OVERVIEW: In connection with divorce proceedings, appellant ex-wife and respondent ex-husband executed a marital settlement agreement which included a provision in which they warranted to one another that neither was possessed of any property other than what was listed in the agreement, and that if it should later be determined that either was possessed of any property not set forth in the agreement, each agreed to pay one-half of the fair market value of such property to the other. Several years after the divorce was final, appellant brought an order to show cause proceeding in the original divorce action, seeking to enforce the marital settlement agreement as to respondent's military pension, which he had begun collecting since the divorce. The trial court ruled against appellant. On appeal, the court affirmed on the basis that the trial court had no jurisdiction to consider appellant's claims in the modification proceeding. However, the court held that the pension rights could be adjudicated in a separate independent action, and that the contract between the parties governed the pension issue. A court reviewing the agreement was bound to enforce the rights created therein.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant ex-wife's order to show cause in a divorce proceeding, which requested payment of one-half of respondent ex-husband's military pension, because the divorce was final and the trial court had no jurisdiction to consider the issue; however, the court ruled that the issue could be raised in a separate proceeding.

 

1952 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harvey


Crim. No. 29952


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


76 Cal. App. 3d 441; 142 Cal. Rptr. 887; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1141



January 3, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 2, 1978. Beach, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted. The Petitions of Both Parties for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied March 2, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 320920, E. Talbot Callister, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The sentence on count I is modified to impose imprisonment in state prison for life. The sentences on the remaining counts are merged into the life term and ordered to run concurrently with it. As modified, the judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was transferred from the Supreme Court (California) for modification of appellant's sentence of death imposed for killing a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder for killing a police officer and was given the death penalty. In accordance with case law, the Supreme Court transferred the case for modification of appellant's sentence. Appellant contended that his accusation by grand jury indictment instead of by information was unconstitutional in that it denied him the fundamental right of a preliminary hearing at a "critical phase" of the proceedings, in violation of due process and equal protection of law. California courts had already rejected appellant's argument that grand jury accusation without opportunity for preliminary hearing was unconstitutional in other case law. The people contended that appellant should be returned to the trial court for resentencing under the newly adopted death penalty statute. Under the sequence of events in the case, the reviewing court concluded that such an increase in sentence would put appellant in jeopardy of his life a second time. The court modified appellant's sentence to life in prison in the state court. Because of its reduction in appellant's sentence, the court had to modify appellant's other sentences by merging them in to the life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court modified appellant's sentence to life in state prison and merged sentences for other convictions into the life sentence because the court found that only life imprisonment could be constitutionally imposed under the death penalty law under which appellant was sentenced.

 

1953 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Apodaca


Crim. No. 2827


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


76 Cal. App. 3d 479; 142 Cal. Rptr. 830; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1145



January 3, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On February 2, 1978, the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 2, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 29418, Leonard Irving Meyers and Simon Marootian, Judges.



DISPOSITION: As so modified, the judgment is affirmed. The trial court hereby is directed to prepare an amended abstract of judgment reflecting the above modification and to deliver a copy of the amended abstract of judgment to the Department of Corrections. The Department of Corrections hereby is directed to amend appellant's commitment record to conform with this opinion, and to reflect the new commitment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for the murder of a human fetus under Cal. Penal Code § 187, and of the sentences he received for that conviction and his convictions of rape under Cal. Penal Code § 261(3), and assault under Cal. Penal Code § 245(a), entered in the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), asserting that the murder statute was vague and that he received impermissible multiple punishment under Cal. Penal Code § 654.


OVERVIEW: After talking with his ex-wife and disavowing the fetus she was carrying, appellant announced his intent to kill the fetus. Appellant repeatedly struck his ex-wife in the abdomen and raped her, causing her to bleed. Several weeks later, she gave birth to a dead fetus. An expert testified that the death was due to a partial separation of the placenta from the cervix, which could result from a physical trauma inflicted on the mother. Appellant was convicted of the murder of a human fetus, rape by threats of great and immediate bodily harm, and assault by means of force likely to produce great bodily injury, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code §§ 189, 261(3), 245(a), respectively. The court affirmed his convictions, holding that the murder statute was not unconstitutionally vague because a person of common intelligence could reasonably understand what was proscribed. However, the court agreed with appellant that he had been subjected to multiple punishment, finding that he could not be punished for both the rape and the assault because both were part of an indivisible course of conduct intended to kill the fetus. Thus, it modified the judgment to stay the assault sentence.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to stay appellant's assault sentence pending the finality of its judgment and the service of his rape sentence, with the stay to become permanent when service of sentence as to the rape count was completed. As modified, the court affirmed, rejecting appellant's argument that the murder statute was impermissibly vague as applied to the murder of a human fetus.

 

1954 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Department of Corrections v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


Civ. No. 17127


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


77 Cal. App. 3d 610; 143 Cal. Rptr. 767; 1978 Cal. App. LEXIS 1243; 43 Cal. Comp. Cases 169



Feb. 7, 1978 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Apr. 6, 1978 (see 23 C.3d 197)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, corrections department, sought review of an order from the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which awarded death benefits to respondent widow and decedent's minor child of a prior marriage.


OVERVIEW: The court annulled the death benefit award of respondent, Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (Board), that was made on behalf of respondent widow and the decedent's minor child of a prior marriage. The court held that under Cal. Lab. Code § 4707 there could be no award under the Workers' Compensation Law when a widow or minor child would receive an award under the State Employees' Retirement System, which would be equal or greater to the award under the compensation law. The court annulled the award because it found that respondent Board had erroneously made two awards: one under the Workers' Compensation Law and the second under the Retirement System, and the award was in direct conflict with § 4707. The court found that respondent widow had failed to sustain her burden of proof on her constitutional challenge of § 4707 because she failed to demonstrate the invalidity of the classification within the statute.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the death benefit award that had been made on behalf of respondent widow and the minor child of decedent because respondent, Workers' Compensation Appeals Board had improperly made two awards under the Workers' Compensation Law and the State Employees' Retirement System.

 

1955 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schuler


Crim. No. 15838


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


76 Cal. App. 3d 324; 142 Cal. Rptr. 798; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2111



December 29, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, Nos. 45857, 46169 and 47259, Alan A. Lindsay, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We therefore order that the cause be remanded to the trial court with direction to amend the judgments in each of the above cases in conformity with this opinion.

This opinion does not in any way affect the judgment imposed in information No. 54911.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentence he received for multiple convictions, entered in the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), asserting that he was entitled to credit under Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5, the Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Cal. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 15, for time spent in prison on two earlier counts that had subsequently been dismissed as part of a second plea bargain into which he entered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with 11 felony offenses while incarcerated. He entered a guilty plea to two of the offenses; the remaining charges were dismissed. While on parole, four counts of robbery were brought against him. While imprisoned a second time, he brought a successful writ of habeas corpus challenging the offenses that originally landed him in prison. The original 11 charges were reinstated. He then entered a second plea bargain for the original 11 offenses, pleading guilty to four of them. Defendant was sentenced to prison and was given credit for time spent as an unsentenced prisoner. He claimed he was entitled to credit for his time in prison on the two counts that were subsequently dismissed as part of the second plea bargain. The court agreed, remanding the case with direction to amend the judgments on the offenses to conform to its opinion. Defendant was entitled to credit under Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5, Cal. Const. art. I, §§7, 15, and the principles of fair play inherent in the Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court rejected defendant's claim that he was entitled to credit under Cal. Penal Code § 2900.1 because the same criminal acts were not at issue.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause with direction to amend the judgment in the various cases against defendant to conform to its opinion, agreeing with defendant that he was entitled to credit for time served on charges that were later dismissed pursuant to a plea bargain.

 

1956 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Rees v. Department of Real Estate


Civ. No. 39546


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


76 Cal. App. 3d 286; 142 Cal. Rptr. 789; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2108



December 29, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 690738, Byron Arnold, Judge. *


* Retired judge of the superior court sitting under assignment by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant businessman challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that denied his petition for a writ of mandate to direct respondent Department of Real Estate to vacate its order that appellant refrain from performing certain activities without first obtaining a real estate license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant businessman challenged a judgment of the trial court denying his petition for a writ of mandate to direct respondent Department of Real Estate to vacate its order that appellant refrain from performing certain activities without first obtaining a real estate license. The trial court found that appellant acted in the capacity of a real estate licensee and violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 10130. In his challenged, appellant contested the sufficiency and propriety of the findings and whether the real estate licensing statutes and regulations could be validly applied to his business activities. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the record amply supported the finding that appellant, without being validly licensed, solicited listings of non-owned rentals and prospective tenants for compensation or in expectation of compensation. The court further determined that the finder's exception to the licensing requirement did not apply as appellant did merely introduce landlords and tenants. Finally, the court held that the licensing statutes did not violate U.S. Const. amend V or U.S. Const. amend XIV.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the record supported the finding that appellant businessman solicited listings of non-owned rentals and prospective tenants for compensation without being licensed, and appellant did not merely introduce landlords and tenants. Further, the licensing statutes did not violate appellant's due process or equal protection rights.

1958 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Lyons v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 17629


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


75 Cal. App. 3d 829; 142 Cal. Rptr. 449; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2061



December 7, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified December 16, 1977. A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 27, 1977, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 1, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 255735, Kenneth E. Lae, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Jugdment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Superior Court, Orange County (California) in an action by appellant for a writ of prohibition or mandate to the trial court, which the superior court had denied. Appellant's probation had been revoked, and he had been sentenced to jail for his previous conviction of violating Cal. Penal Code § 270, failure to provide for his minor children.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with failure to provide for his minor children, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 270. He pled guilty and was placed on probation. Appellant thereafter was found to have been in violation of his probation and was ordered to jail. Appellant sought a writ of prohibition/mandate in superior court, which was denied. Appellant contended that superior court jurisdiction precluded municipal court jurisdiction; his prosecution denied him equal protection of the law; imprisonment for violating § 270 constituted imprisonment for a debt; § 270 was vague and uncertain; and failure to charge the custodial mother constituted invidious discrimination. The court affirmed. The legislature conferred upon the municipal court jurisdiction over criminal cases amounting to a misdemeanor within the ambit of § 270. Appellant was not deprived of equal protection of the law. Where issues, including defenses, may differ in different proceedings, such was not sufficient, without more, to show a denial of equal protection. The statutory obligation of a parent to support his or her minor child was not a debt, and a prosecution under § 270 was not a civil action for debt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's denial of a writ of prohibition or mandate to the trial court, following the trial court's order revoking appellant's probation and sentencing him to jail, because the trial court had jurisdiction to find him guilty and sentence him to incarceration. His prosecution did not constitute a violation of equal protection, and he had not been sentenced for a debt.

 

1959 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Payne


Crim. No. 16544


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


75 Cal. App. 3d 601; 142 Cal. Rptr. 320; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2037



December 1, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 1, 1977, and the Petitions of both Parties for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied January 19, 1978.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People filed a petition seeking a rehearing by the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), asserting that defendant's case should have been remanded for a hearing under newly enacted Cal. Penal Code § 190.3 to determine whether the penalty should have been death or life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder with a finding of special circumstances which led to a sentence of death. The case was assigned to this court for disposition following a decision which found certain statute unconstitutional. The court modified the judgment of conviction to impose a life sentence instead of the penalty of death. By petition for rehearing, the People asserted that the case should have been remanded for a hearing to determine whether the penalty should have been death or life imprisonment without possibility of parole under the provisions of newly enacted Cal. Penal Code § 190.3. The court found that the new statute demonstrably inflicted greater punishment than could have been inflicted under the former statute at the time the act was committed. Denying the petition for rehearing, the court held that the statute adopting a new scheme could not have been applied to defendant who was tried and sentenced under the former law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the People's petition for rehearing on the ground that the new statute relating to punishment could not have been applied to defendant's case, because the statute was not in effect when he committed the offense.
