Redevelopment Agency v. Shepard


Civ. No. 40332


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


75 Cal. App. 3d 453; 142 Cal. Rptr. 212; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2026



November 29, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Hearing granted August 11, 1977 (L.A. 30827). Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 26, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 161633, Samuel W. Hall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We conclude that a referendum is not required. Accordingly, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant director challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which validated a proposed issuance of revenue bonds to finance a redevelopment project.


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed an in rem proceeding to validate the proposed bond issue. The redevelopment plan (plan) called for conversion of a blighted area into a residential development which would include low-density residential, multi-family residential, and commercial areas. The trial court validated the proposed issuance. On appeal, the court determined that the plan did not involve a gift of public funds or an improper use of a public credit in violation of the state constitution. The proposed bonds were expenditures for public purposes. Providing decent housing for the public was a public purpose. There was no unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to respondent. Lastly, the proposed bond issue did not require voter approval, because the project was one that was developed, constructed or acquired with the meaning of the state constitution. The judgment was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that validated a proposed issuance of revenue bonds to finance a redevelopment project was affirmed, because the plan did not violate state constitutional provisions and involved a public purpose.

 

1962 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Lattin v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 40669


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


75 Cal. App. 3d 377; 142 Cal. Rptr. 130; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2021



November 25, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 23, 1977, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 26, 1978. Bird, C. J., Tobriner, J., and Richardson, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 702451, John E. Benson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The orders from which plaintiffs have appealed are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his motion that a class action was proper and to certify a class of taxpayers, to be represented by appellant, in his claim that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 17069(f) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer paid his state income taxes under protest, claiming that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 17069(f), which allowed a special tax credit to California income taxpayers residing in the state for a full year, but denied it for others who were not residents at the close of the tax year. After his claim for refund was denied by respondent Franchise Tax Board and denied again on appeal by the State Board of Equalization, appellant brought suit as a class action for recovery of personal income tax paid under protest, purporting to represent all others similarly situated. The trial court held that appellant's action was invalid as a class action. If the Legislature has imposed prerequisites to an action against the state or one of its agencies, those conditions must be strictly complied with. It is a condition to filing suit against the Franchise Tax Board to have first filed a claim for refund, per Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 19051- 19064. Appellant filed his claim only on his own behalf, not on behalf of the class; therefore, he could not file a suit to recover on behalf of the class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant taxpayer's motion to certify a class of taxpayers to be represented by appellant. The court held that appellant's failure to claim a refund from respondent Franchise Tax Board on behalf of the class foreclosed his ability to bring the action to claim the refund on the class' behalf.

 

1963 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Marvin F. v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 41397


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


75 Cal. App. 3d 281; 142 Cal. Rptr. 78; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2011



November 22, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 22, 1977, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. The Petition of the Real Party in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 19, 1978.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandamus is granted, and the cause is remanded to the juvenile court with directions to dismiss the petition to declare Marvin F. a ward of the court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile challenged the decision of respondent, the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which found that the prosecuting attorney's determination to have petitioner declared a ward of the state was proper.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner juvenile was arrested for loitering about a junior high school. Pursuant to an agreement between the probation department and the district attorney, the intake juvenile probation officer presented the matter to the prosecuting attorney, who filed a petition seeking wardship. On appeal, petitioner sought an order directing a dismissal of the juvenile court proceedings. The court found that juvenile matters were only properly before the prosecuting attorney for determination of wardship if the probation officer requested the prosecuting attorney to take such action by presenting him with an affidavit. Furthermore, the initial determination to file could not be delegated to the prosecuting attorney because it was a judgment expressly vested in the probation department under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 7. Therefore, the court found that the agreement conflicted with the statutory scheme for processing applications for wardship in juvenile court. The petition for writ of mandamus was granted, and the cause was remanded to the juvenile court with directions to dismiss the petition to declare petitioner a ward of the court.


OUTCOME: Respondent trial court's decision, which found that prosecuting attorney's determination to have petitioner declared a ward of the state, was reversed. The court concluded that the determination to file wardship petitions was vested in the probation department and could only be delegated upon request by affidavit.

 

1964 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Leonard R.


Crim. No. 30289


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


76 Cal. App. 3d 100; 142 Cal. Rptr. 632; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2087



November 21, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 19, 1978. Bird, C. J., Tobriner, J., and Newman, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. J251143, Robert H. Fletcher, Referee.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that adjudged him delinquent and committed him to the California Youth Authority. Defendant claimed that he was entitled to a new dispositional hearing to establish that a knife was not used in the robbery for which he was charged, and that he was entitled to presentence credit for time spent in juvenile hall while criminal proceedings were pending.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was committed to the California Youth Authority, he contended he was entitled to credit against his commitment for time spent in juvenile hall while the juvenile proceedings against him were pending. Defendant also argued that he was entitled to a new dispositional hearing to establish that a knife was not used in the robbery for which he was charged. On review, the court held that presentence credit did not apply to the juvenile court system. A declaration of wardship was not a "conviction," and a dispositional order of the juvenile court was not a "sentence" within the meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 2900.5. The denial of presentence credit to juveniles was not unconstitutional because the distinction between adults and juveniles clearly bore a substantial relationship to a legitimate legislative objective. Defendant's commitment was not an abuse of discretion because it was not based on the nature of the weapon that was used, but on defendant's anti-social behavior as demonstrated by his participation in a robbery after he had participated in three prior robberies and an assault. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendant's commitment was based upon his anti-social behavior as demonstrated by his repeated criminal acts, and not upon the exact nature of the weapon that was used in the robbery for which he was charged. Presentence credit was not permitted because a valid distinction existed between juveniles and adults, and juveniles were not "convicted" or "sentenced" within the meaning of the criminal code.

 

1965 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Salton City Etc. Owners Assn. v. M. Penn Phillips Co.


Civ. No. 50488


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


75 Cal. App. 3d 184; 141 Cal. Rptr. 895; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2001



November 18, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 16, 1977, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 19, 1978. Clark, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-145893, Charles H. Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is reversed and the cause remanded with directions to the superior court to vacate said order of dismissal and overrule Phillips' demurrer. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners association challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained respondent seller's demurrer to appellant's complaint for damages or rescission and restitution of land sale contracts and dismissed the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowners association challenged the trial court's decision granting respondent seller's demurrer and dismissing appellant's complaint for misrepresentation due to lack of standing. Appellant brought suit in its representative capacity on behalf of its members. Respondent claimed that an action had to be prosecuted in the name of the real party in interest unless it was a public interest case and sought only prospective relief. The court determined that this was a class action on behalf of a self-defined class. The class represented in the action was readily ascertainable. The commonality of the questions of law and fact involved in the action, the community of interest, was adequately set forth in the complaint which alleged the use of a fraudulent canned sales pitch which was designed to and did induce the members to purchase property in a common area. The court held that the trial court would have to inquire into the nature and scope of appellant's authorization to determine whether the action should be permitted to proceed in its present format. The court reversed and remanded the case with directions to vacate the dismissal and overrule respondent's demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting respondent seller's demurrer and dismissing appellant homeowners association's complaint for fraudulent misrepresentation and directed the court to vacate the dismissal. The court held that appellant in its representative capacity was bringing suit on behalf of its members in a class action suit on behalf of a self-defined class.

 

1966 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Hogya v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 16727


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


75 Cal. App. 3d 122; 142 Cal. Rptr. 325; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1996



November 16, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 2, 1977, and the Petition of the Real Parties in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 10, 1978. Clark, J., Richardson, J., and Manuel, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue compelling the San Diego County Superior Court to (1) vacate its order denying petitioner's motion for class certification and (2) grant the motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), that denied his order for class certification in his action seeking compensatory and punitive damages and injunctive relief pursuant to the Consumers Legal Remedies Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 1750 et seq., on behalf of himself and others that purchased falsely upgraded beef.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought review after his motion for class certification, in his action seeking relief pursuant to the Consumers Legal Remedies Act (act), Cal. Civ. Code § 1750, was denied. The court granted petitioner's petition for writ of mandamus, and reversed the decision denying class certification. The court found that its intervention was warranted via petitioner's request for an extraordinary writ because the issue raised was substantial and one of first impression. The court found that Cal. Civ. Code § 1781(b) established exclusive criteria for class certification in suits brought pursuant to the act. Based upon the common meaning of "shall" as used in statutes, the clear directive of § 1752 that actions brought pursuant to the act were to be governed exclusively by its own provisions, and the frustration of the act's purposes and effectiveness which would result from a contrary interpretation, the court concluded the use of the word "shall" in § 1781(b) had to be given a mandatory meaning. Because petitioner met the criteria contained in § 1782, the lower court did not have any discretion to deny class certification.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate compelling the lower court to vacate its order denying petitioner's motion for class certification and to grant the motion holding that the applicable statute established exclusive criteria for class certification in suits brought pursuant to the Consumers Legal Remedies Act, and that if the statutory criteria was satisfied, a trial court was under a duty to certify the class.

 

1967 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bowers v. City of San Buenaventura


Civ. No. 49707


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


75 Cal. App. 3d 65; 142 Cal. Rptr. 35; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1988



November 15, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 8, 1977, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 13, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. SP 47922, Robert Lee Shaw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The matter is reversed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in this opinion. The parties to pay their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which entered a judgment granting a peremptory writ of mandate to compel defendant to pay salary and to follow certain personnel procedures on account of temporary military leave for plaintiff employee, pursuant to Cal. Mil. & Vet. Code § 395.01.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee, a member of the National Guard, took temporary military leaves of absence from his employment with defendant city. Defendant required that its employees, in order to keep both military and regular pay for periods of military leave, work on days that would otherwise have been days off. Plaintiff did so for most of the days of leave, but was not paid by defendant for a number of days which he did not make up and for which he did not turn over his military pay to defendant. Plaintiff sought a peremptory writ of mandate to require defendant to grant him military leave, and pay him, in accordance with Cal. Mil. & Vet. Code § 395.01. The trial court granted the writ, and defendant sought review. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that because § 395.01 reflected a matter of statewide concern overriding city charters, it could constitutionally be applied to defendant. The court held, though, that the trial court had erred in failing to distinguish active military training, to which defendant could not apply its policy, from weekend drills, which the legislature had eliminated from the scope of § 395.01.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate requiring defendant city to pay salary and follow personnel procedures on account of plaintiff employee's military leaves, because while the military leave statute was applicable to defendant, it did not cover weekend drills.

 

1968 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Woodland Hills Residents Ass'n v. City Council of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 48207


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION Four


75 Cal. App. 3d 1; 141 Cal. Rptr. 857; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1982; 8 ELR 20046



November 14, 1977 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Jan. 26, 1978 (see 23 C.3d 917)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, association and members, sought review of a decision of a trial court (California), which denied them an award of attorney's fees in their mandamus action to require respondents, municipal agencies, to vacate their decisions approving respondent developer's tract map of a proposed subdivision.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, association and members, brought a mandamus action against respondents, municipal agencies, seeking to have each of them vacate its decision approving a tract map of respondent developer's proposed subdivision. The trial court initially entered a judgment against plaintiffs, but the judgment was reversed on appeal. On retrial, the trial court made findings of fact and conclusions of law and entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, but denied plaintiffs an award of attorney's fees. Plaintiffs sought review. The court reversed the portion of the judgment appealed from. The court held that because plaintiffs had conferred a substantial environmental benefit on all the citizens of the municipality, they were entitled to attorney's fees under an exception to the usual rule, set out in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021, that fees would only be awarded if authorized by statute or contract. The court directed, though, that because the benefit to plaintiffs was greater than the benefit to the taxpayers in general, plaintiffs should bear the greater portion of the value of legal services rendered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment denying plaintiffs, association and members, attorney's fees in their mandamus action to require respondents, municipal agencies, to vacate decisions approving respondent developer's tract map of a proposed subdivision, because plaintiffs had conferred a substantial benefit upon the citizens of the municipality. The court directed the award of appropriate attorney's fees.

 

1969 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Privitera


Crim. No. 8323


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION One


74 Cal. App. 3d 936; 141 Cal. Rptr. 764; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1977



November 10, 1977 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Jan. 5, 1978 (see 23 C.3d 697)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, physician and drug suppliers, appealed their convictions for conspiracy to sell or prescribe an unapproved drug intended for the alleviation or cure of cancer, Cal. Penal Code § 182(1), Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1707.1, following proceedings in a California trial court. In addition, two of defendant drug suppliers appealed their separate convictions for selling the unapproved drug.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, physician and drug suppliers, were in involved in a common plan to distribute and prescribe laetrile to cancer patients. They were convicted of conspiring to sell or prescribe an unapproved drug intended for the alleviation or cure of cancer. Cal. Penal Code § 182(1), Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1707.1. Two of defendant suppliers were also convicted of selling laetrile. The court reversed the convictions, finding that § 1707.1 infringed upon defendant physician's patients' fundamental right to choose their medical treatment and that the state did not have a compelling interest in preventing the patients from taking laetrile or in preventing defendant physician from prescribing it. The court thus held that § 1701.1 violated defendant physician's and his patients' privacy rights under U.S. Const. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 1. The court also held that the trial court erred in denying defendants' motion to suppress evidence obtained through a telephonic search warrant because the U.S. Customs agent who signed the magistrate's name to the warrant was not a "peace officer" under California law and was thus not authorized to do so under Cal. Penal Code § 1528.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant physician's and drug suppliers' convictions for conspiring to distribute and prescribe an unapproved drug and for selling an unapproved drug. The statute that criminalized the prescription and distribution of the unapproved drug infringed upon defendant physician's and his patients' privacy rights and the trial court erred in denying defendants' motion to suppress critical evidence.

 

1970 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Schettler v. County of Santa Clara


Civ. No. 40141


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


74 Cal. App. 3d 990; 141 Cal. Rptr. 731; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1979



November 9, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied December 9, 1977, and respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied January 19, 1978. Mosk, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 353633, O. Vincent Bruno, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant importer sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted respondent county summary judgment on an action brought by appellant to recover ad valorem property taxes imposed on imported inventory of appellant. Appellant contended that an amendment to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 226, exempted the goods from the taxes in question.


OVERVIEW: Appellant importer filed an action against respondent county to recover ad valorem property taxes imposed on imported inventory owned by appellant. Respondent imposed the taxes on the basis of the United State Supreme Court's decision in Michelin Tire Corp. v. Wages, 423 U.S. 276, 46 L.Ed.2d 495 (1976), which held ad valorem taxes could be imposed upon imported goods. After Michelin, the legislature revised Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 226, to provide that the court decision would only be applied prospectively. Respondent challenged the constitutionality of the prospective effect of § 226, and the trial court granted summary judgment for respondent. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the amendment to § 226 was constitutional because the legislature could decide whether to allow prospective application of the legal precedent, and its decision to do so did not amount to an unconstitutional gift of public money because the primary purpose of the act was to benefit the public which might otherwise suffer from the unanticipated retroactive imposition of the tax.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment for county was reversed because the statute was constitutional, the legislature had the right to enact legislation mandating prospective application of the decision, and the statute did not amount to an unconstitutional gift of public money.

 

1971 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Jorge S.


Crim. No. 30270


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


74 Cal. App. 3d 852; 141 Cal. Rptr. 722; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1970



November 8, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. J537338, Robert B. Lopez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found him to be a minor violating laws as defined by Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, and adjudged that he had committed a burglary. Defendant argued that the order finding him a juvenile of the court should be reversed because his confession was the result of an illegal arrest and should be suppressed.


OVERVIEW: Police placed defendant in custody for being truant from school. While en route, defendant was informed that he was a suspect in a robbery. At the police station, defendant waived his constitutional rights after being apprised of them and confessed to a burglary of his neighbor's house. At the adjudication hearing, defendant objected to the confession's admission as a result of the exploitation of an unlawful arrest. This objection was overruled and defendant was charged and convicted of burglary. On appeal, defendant argued again that the confession should have been suppressed as a result of an illegal arrest. The court agreed and reversed. The court held that by reviewing the record it was clear that defendant was under arrest. Had police been acting under Cal. Educ. Code §§ 12405, 12406, they had to adhere to statutory requirements, which did not occur. The court reviewed the record and found that no probable cause existed to arrest defendant and no intervening independent act of a free will or other circumstance served to attenuate the taint of the unconstitutional arrest and the resulting confession.


OUTCOME: The court reversed because no probable cause existed to arrest defendant, under the truancy statute he should have been returned to his parents, and the confession arising from his arrest was tainted by his illegal detention and should have been suppressed.

 

1972 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Frisco Land & Mining Co. v. State of California


Civ. No. 39320


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


74 Cal. App. 3d 736; 141 Cal. Rptr. 820; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1964



November 7, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied January 4, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, No. 71226, Joseph G. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land developer sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which granted summary judgment to respondent state. Appellant sought damages for inverse condemnation. He claimed that the state through the acts and omissions of a coastal regulatory commission had taken his land without payment of just compensation. Respondent contended that the restrictions on use of property did not constitute a taking.


OVERVIEW: Appellant land developer was the owner of a subdivision, substantially all of which was embraced within the permit area of the coastal zone created by the California Zone Conservation Act, Cal. Pub. Res. Code §§ 27000- 27650. Appellant contended that the state through passage of the act and the omissions of the regional commission, deprived appellant of the only use he had for his lands, which was the sale of lots for the building of single family homes. Appellant contended that the actions constituted a taking of his property without just compensation. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondent state, holding that there was no taking of land. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the act did not establish any present possessory interest of the people of the state in the property and that the restrictions placed on the use of the property by the act and by the commission did not constitute a taking. The court also held that by withdrawing his permit for a blanket permit, appellant failed to exhaust his administrative remedies and therefore, could not challenge the ruling of an administrative body in court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the California Zone Conservation Act of 1972, which restricted appellant land developer's use of his property, did not constitute a taking without just compensation. The court held that the placing of restrictions on the use of property did not constitute a taking.

 

1973 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


MacDonald v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 51549


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


75 Cal. App. 3d 692; 141 Cal. Rptr. 667; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 2047



November 7, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue requiring the respondeat superior court to vacate so much of its orders dated March 31 and May 26, 1977, as purport to forbid the prosecution of petitioners' appeal from the judgment in the action entitled Satin et al., vs. MacDonald et al., No. SE C 14035. Pending finality of this decision, enforcement of the respondent court's orders of March 31 and May 26, 1977, is stayed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtors sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to overturn an order forbidding defendants to go forward with an appeal from the trial court's judgment in a civil action. The order was a sanction for failure to answer postjudgment interrogatories served under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 714.5.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, the real parties in interest on appeal, obtained a money judgment against defendant debtors, and defendants appealed. When plaintiffs served postjudgment interrogatories on defendants, defendants did not answer and plaintiffs filed a motion to compel answers. The trial court granted the motion and held that defendants would be barred from prosecuting their appeal if they did not answer the interrogatories within 60 days. The trial court then granted defendants' motion to reconsider but decided that the prior order stood. Defendants brought a mandate proceeding to compel the trial court to vacate the order. Defendants contended that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 714.5, which authorized the use of written interrogatories for examining a judgment debtor concerning his property, put debtors at a disadvantage if they were not represented by counsel. The court found that § 714.5 did not discriminate, but the section did not authorize the trial court to prohibit an appeal as a sanction for noncompliance. The court directed the trial court to vacate its orders forbidding the prosecution of defendants' appeal from the judgment in the action brought by plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court directed that a peremptory writ of mandate issue requiring respondent superior court to vacate its orders forbidding defendant debtors to prosecute its appeal because the civil procedure code did not authorize the bar of an appeal as a discovery sanction for defendants' failure to answer postjudgment interrogatories.

 

1974 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


United Farm Workers v. Agricultural Labor Relations Board


Civ. No. 51777


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


74 Cal. App. 3d 347; 141 Cal. Rptr. 437; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1923; 97 L.R.R.M. 2296



October 24, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition of the UFW is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner labor union filed a petition to review the decision of respondent Agricultural Labor Relations Board that found employer had engaged in unfair labor practices, and that denied petitioner's motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner labor union challenged the decision of respondent Agricultural Labor Relations Board (board) that found employer had engaged in unfair labor practices. Petitioner first filed a motion for reconsideration which was denied by respondent. Petitioner then filed its petition about 69 days after respondent's orders were issued. The court dismissed the petition because it determined that the time to seek judicial review of an administrative decision is jurisdictional. Cal. Lab. Code § 1160.8 required that the petition be filed within 30 days from the date of the issuance of the board's order. Respondent's orders were final orders because they directed a remedy for unfair labor practices pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 1160.8. Since motions for reconsideration did not operate to stay the action of respondent the petition was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition to review as untimely because the time to seek judicial review of an administrative decision was jurisdictional. The statute required that the petition be filed within 30 days from the date of the issuance of respondent Agricultural Labor Relations Board's order. Respondent's orders were final orders because they directed a remedy for unfair labor practices.

 

1975 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Way v. Superior Court of San Diego County


Civ. Nos. 16970, 16971


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


74 Cal. App. 3d 165; 141 Cal. Rptr. 383; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1905



October 19, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On November 10, 1977, the opinion was modified to read as printed above. The petition of the real parties in interest for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 22, 1977. Clark, J., and Richardson, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ issue directing the respondent courts to vacate their preliminary injunctions and to dismiss the petitions of real parties in interest.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner agencies sought review of the decisions of respondents, the Superior Court of San Diego County and the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted real party in interest taxpayers and real party in interest judicial and law enforcement officials' requests for a preliminary injunction preventing the retroactive application of provisions of the Uniform Determinate Sentencing Act of 1976, Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2.


OVERVIEW: Real party in interest taxpayers and real party in interest judicial and law enforcement officials filed actions in the trial courts for preliminary injunctions preventing the retroactive application of the Uniform Determinate Sentencing Act of 1976 (UDSA), Cal. Penal Code § 1170.2. The parties alleged that the UDSA was a legislative infringement upon the governor's power to commute sentences under Cal. Const. art. V, § 8 and that it violated the separation of powers clause of the Cal. Const. art. III, § 3. Respondent trial courts granted the real parties' motions, and petitioner state agencies sought review. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that retroactive application of the UDSA did not constitute an unconstitutional usurpation of the governor's commutation power. While § 1170.2 has the effect of commutation in certain cases, an action outside the scope of the legislature's power, the shortening of existing prison terms by the UDSA was purely incidental to the main legislative purpose, and thus the UDSA was not unconstitutional. There could be no complete separation of powers of government in an ever-changing social order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions granting a preliminary injunction, finding that retroactive application of the Uniform Determinate Sentencing Act (UDSA) did not constitute an unconstitutional usurpation of the governor's commutation power. While the pertinent section had the effect of commutation in certain cases, a power reserved to the governor, the shortening of existing prison terms was purely incidental to the main legislative purpose.

People v. Shepherd


Crim. No. 30932


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


74 Cal. App. 3d 334; 141 Cal. Rptr. 379; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1921



October 19, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 7, 1977, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 15, 1977. Bird, C. J., Mosk, J., and Richardson, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. 31534109, Alan G. Campbell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of offering to sell three football tickets on the premises of the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum in violation of Los Angeles Municipal Code § 63.51.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Los Angeles Municipal Code § 63.51 for offering to sell three extra football tickets on the premises of the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum without written consent from the Board of Recreation. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed his conviction. The court found that, although defendant's conduct seemed harmless, an ordinance that attempted to distinguish between the casual vendor and commercial operator would be ineffective due to practical problems of identification. The court ruled that § 63.51was not unconstitutional because the limitation upon the use of the park for sales solicitation was a reasonable place limitation based upon significant governmental interest. The court determined that the purpose of § 63.51was not to regulate ticket sales but limit business activity on public property dedicated to recreational use; as use of a city park is a municipal matter, Cal. Penal Code § 346 did not preempt the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for offering to sell football tickets upon the premises of the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum because the ordinance governing the sale of merchandise in public parks was constitutional.

 

1977 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Schmier v. Board of Trustees


Civ. No. 16304


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


74 Cal. App. 3d 314; 141 Cal. Rptr. 472; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1918; 16 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 195; 15 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8025



October 18, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 15, 1977. Mosk, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 373864, Daniel C. Leedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff professor appealed an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which dismissed plaintiff's petition for writ of mandate without leave to amend after a general demurrer by defendants, Board of Trustees of the California State University and Colleges and others, was sustained.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff professor filed a petition with the trial court for a writ of mandate against defendants, Board of Trustees of the California State University and Colleges and others, when defendants, pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 20981, terminated plaintiff's contract as an assistant professor when he attained the mandatory retirement age of 67. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer without leave to amend, and dismissed plaintiff's petition. Plaintiff contended he had a contractual right to employment to age 70, that his termination at age 67 was a breach of contract, and that the statutory establishment of a mandatory retirement age was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's petition, and held that plaintiff's employment as an assistant professor with tenure was a statutory right under Cal. Gov't Code § 20981 and was not a matter of contract, that the Legislature could reduce the tenure of plaintiff's position when it changed the mandatory retirement age from 70 to 67, and that the statutory establishment of mandatory retirement was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the demurrer by defendants, board of trustees and others, of plaintiff professor's petition for a writ of mandate because plaintiff's employment was a statutory right and not a matter of contract. The court held that the reduction of plaintiff's tenure when the legislature reduced the mandatory retirement age from 70 to 67 was valid, and that the statutory establishment of mandatory retirement was not unconstitutional.

 

1978 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Hawn v. County of Ventura


Civ. No. 48220


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


73 Cal. App. 3d 1009; 141 Cal. Rptr. 111; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1836



October 7, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 27, 1977, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 15, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. SP 47737, Richard C. Heaton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city and plaintiff city residents challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Ventura County (California), which was entered in favor of defendant county, defendant county board of supervisors, defendant county officials, and defendant county residents and which declared unconstitutional an ordinance which sought to place restrictions on the location of new airports in the county.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city and plaintiff city residents sought a writ of mandate, as well as injunctive and declaratory relief, to enforce an ordinance which restricted the location of new airports in the county. Defendant county, defendant county board of supervisors, defendant county officials, and defendant county residents maintained that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment in defendants' favor and declared the ordinance unconstitutional. Plaintiffs appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. Applying a strict standard of review, the court held that the ordinance violated the equal protection clause of both the U.S. and California Constitutions, in that it approved an invidious discrimination against non-city voters in the county. The ordinance conferred upon voters within city limits the opportunity to vote on the location of an airport, but denied that same right to persons living outside the cities even though the location of an airport was a local environmental issue impacting voters within the city limits, as well as voters living outside the city limits. Further, there was no compelling interest justifying the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which was entered in favor of defendant county, defendant county board of supervisors, defendant county officials, and defendant county residents and which declared unconstitutional an ordinance restricting the location of new airports in the county. Contrary to the claims of plaintiff city and plaintiff city residents, the ordinance contained an unconstitutional voting scheme.

 

1979 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Katz v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 41045


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


73 Cal. App. 3d 952; 141 Cal. Rptr. 234; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1833



October 6, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied November 4, 1977, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. The petition of the real parties in interest for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 15, 1977. Mosk, J., and Clark, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.



DISPOSITION: The petition is granted with respect to petitioners Hovard, Jr., and Kaplan. Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing the respondeat superior court to set aside and vacate its orders appointing temporary conservators for each of said petitioners and the letters of temporary conservatorship issued thereon. Subject to the payment of costs by their respective conservators, the petitions of petitioners Katz, Underwood and Brown are dismissed. Costs of the joint petitions are assessed jointly and severally against the several real parties in interest as they may be taxed in the trial court upon the filing of the remittitur. The order to show cause re contempt issued April 5, 1977, is discharged. The prayer for attorneys' fees is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner adult conservatees sought extraordinary relief in the nature of prohibition and mandamus from orders of respondent Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which appointed their parents as temporary conservators, real parties in interest herein.


OVERVIEW: The court granted relief to petitioner adult conservatees from the trial court's orders appointing their parents temporary conservators. The court held that, to the extent the conservatorship under Cal. Prob. Code § 1751 permitted restraint of an adult's person, it was unconstitutionally vague because it allowed for conservatorship over adults "likely to be deceived or imposed upon by artful or designing persons" which, while susceptible to measurement with regard to property, was incapable of measure as to individuals involved in religious, social, or political causes. The court held that, if adult persons are less than gravely disabled, there was no warrant for depriving them of liberty. The orders further violated petitioners' rights to freedom of religion and association under U.S. Const. amend I and Cal. Const. art. I because, while the state had a compelling interest in preventing fraud under the guise of religious belief and an interest in its citizens' health, in the absence of actions rendering the adult believer gravely disabled, the processes of the state could not be used to deprive the believer of freedom of action and subject to involuntary treatment.


OUTCOME: Following voluntary dismissal by three petitioner conservatees, the court granted the petition as to the two remaining petitioner adult conservatees, directing respondent trial court to set aside and vacate its orders appointing temporary conservators for petitioners. The court held that, if adult persons are less than gravely disabled, there was no warrant for depriving them of liberty.

Schroeder v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 49806


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


73 Cal. App. 3d 841; 141 Cal. Rptr. 85; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1823



October 3, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified October 13, 1977. Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 1, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 155151, Arthur K. Marshall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a licensed amateur radio station operation, challenged an order from respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that denied a peremptory writ of prohibition to enjoin prosecution of a municipal zoning ordinance violation.


OVERVIEW: This was an appeal from a judgment denying a peremptory writ of prohibition directed against respondent municipal court to enjoin prosecution of a municipal zoning ordinance violation. The ordinance in question prohibited in the single family residential zones any radio or television transmitting or receiving antenna over 40 feet in height from the ground or 15 feet from the roof, whichever was less. Appellant was a FCC licensed amateur radio station operator being prosecuted for having constructed at his home a 70 foot vertical antenna. Appellant argued that the ordinance was an invalid regulation of appellant's freedom of speech and expression under U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. Reasonable, narrowly drawn statutes could regulate the time, place, and manner of expression, but blanket prohibitions of expression were invalid as were overbroad statutes or those without clear standards. The judgment was affirmed because the ordinance was constitutional as it did not restrict amateur radio transmission throughout the city, but only in the residential zone and it did not prohibit all transmission even there.


OUTCOME: The denial of a peremptory writ of prohibition to enjoin the prosecution of a municipal zoning ordinance violation was affirmed because the restrictions placed upon appellant by the ordinance were reasonable. The ordinance that regulated radio and television antennas in a residential area was constitutional.

1982 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bratis


Crim. No. 16033


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


73 Cal. App. 3d 751; 141 Cal. Rptr. 45; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1815



September 29, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 25, 1977. Bird, C. J., and Mosk, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. C 6197, Alan W. Haverty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The orders admitting defendants to probation are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an order from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) convicting them of conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 19666, 19667, which prohibited and punished as misdemeanors the alteration or counterfeiting of any pari-mutuel ticket, and the possession of any altered, forged, or counterfeit pari-mutuel ticket. Defendants also challenged their sentences of probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 19666, 19667, which prohibited and punished as misdemeanors the alteration or counterfeiting of any pari-mutuel ticket, and the possession of any altered, forged, or counterfeit pari-mutuel ticket. Defendants were sentenced to probation. On appeal, the court affirmed their convictions and sentences, finding that the convictions were supported by substantial evidence. The court further found that there was ample evidence to connect each of the defendants with the other, and each was observed engaging in activities which contributed to the end for which the altered pari-mutuel tickets obviously would have been used. The jury was instructed fully and properly on the elements of conspiracy. The special findings, that each conspired to commit the substantive crime of which he was also found guilty, could not be interpreted as other than a finding of guilt on the conspiracy charge. Accordingly, the court held that there had been no miscarriage of justice.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions for conspiracy and sentences of probation were affirmed because the convictions were supported by substantial evidence and because the jury was instructed fully and properly on the elements of conspiracy.

 

1983 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Lostritto v. Southern Pac. Transportation Co.


Civ. Nos. 37728, 38388


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


73 Cal. App. 3d 737; 140 Cal. Rptr. 905; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1814



September 28, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 28, 1977, and the petition of the plaintiff and appellant for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 15, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County, No. 49522, Charles S. Franich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order granting new trial on the willful misconduct issue is affirmed, and defendant's appeal from the judgment is dismissed. The order denying judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the willful misconduct issue is affirmed. The negligence count is ordered dismissed. The petition for writ of certiorari is denied and the alternative writ is discharged. Each party will bear its own costs on the appeal and the special proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an injured minor, and defendant railroad both challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County (California), which denied defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and granted defendant's motion for a new trial in plaintiff's action for negligence and willful misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an injured minor, dived into a river from a trestle owned by defendant railroad and was rendered a quadriplegic. Plaintiff filed a complaint against defendant for negligence and willful misconduct. A jury rendered a verdict in favor of plaintiff. However, the trial court granted defendant's motion for a new trial on the issue of willful misconduct. On review, the court found that because it was well known that people dived off of the trestle, defendant was charged with notice of a dangerous condition which existed for a long time. However, the court also found that Cal. Civil Code § 846 stated that an owner of an estate in real property owes no duty of care to keep the premises safe for use by others for a number of activities, including water sports. Thus, because defendant was the owner of the estate, and diving was a water sport, the court found that defendant could not be held liable for failure to use ordinary care in the keeping of the premises or in the matter of warning. Accordingly, the order granting a new trial on the willful misconduct issue was affirmed, and the negligence count was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that denied defendant railroad's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and granted defendant's motion for a new trial in plaintiff's action for negligence and willful misconduct was affirmed. The court held that the applicable statute provided that there was no duty of care to individuals, such as plaintiff, who came onto the land of another for the purpose of, among other things, water sports.

 

1984 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Di Suvero v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 50713


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


73 Cal. App. 3d 718; 140 Cal. Rptr. 895; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1884



September 27, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 1, 1977, rule 27(e), California Rules of Court. Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 25, 1977. Bird, C. J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-177530, Robert I. Weil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged an order entered by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that dismissed his taxpayer's action brought pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 526a without leave to amend. Plaintiff claimed that an in propria persona petition required from pro se criminal defendants infringed on an accused's constitutional and statutory rights.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer claimed that a petition form which defendants in criminal cases completed if they represented themselves was an illegal judicial action that infringed on an accused's constitutional and statutory rights. The taxpayer's action plaintiff brought against defendants, the presiding judges of the criminal and superior courts and the County of Los Angeles, to enjoin expenditure of public funds to implement the court petition policy embodied in a propria persona petition was dismissed without leave to amend. On review, the court held that defendants' demurrer was properly sustained. Although a taxpayer's action under Cal. Civ. Code § 526a addressed governmental action which would otherwise go unchallenged in the courts because of the standing requirement, a criminal defendant had standing and an immediate and plenary recourse within the judicial system with respect to any claimed violation of his constitutional rights. The claim against the county was also unconstitutional because it undermined the independence of the judiciary. Accordingly, the order of dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order that dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's action against respondents, the presiding judges of the criminal and superior courts and the County of Los Angeles, without leave to amend was affirmed. A taxpayer's action was unnecessary to address alleged violations of a criminal defendant's constitutional rights because criminal defendants had standing and an immediate recourse within the judicial system.

 

1985 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Whitcombe v. County of Yolo


Civ. No. 16225


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


73 Cal. App. 3d 698; 141 Cal. Rptr. 189; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1883



September 26, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 24, 1977, and appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 25, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Yolo County, No. 32425, Harry Albright Ackley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's judgment of dismissal is affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant assault victims challenged an order entered by the Superior Court of Yolo County (California) that sustained respondent probation department's demurrer to appellants' action for damages sustained from assault by a probation violator who was released on bail. Appellants claimed that respondents did not determine if the released defendant was a danger to society and that a special relationship between the parties was breached.


OVERVIEW: Appellant assault victims were severely injured when a defendant violated probation and was released on bail. Appellants sought damages from respondent probation department because it neglected to investigate the defendant's criminal activities or determine whether he was a danger to society and breached a special relationship that arose when appellants helped respondents investigate a theft committed by the released defendant. Respondents' demurrer was sustained. On review, the court held that appellants failed to state a cause of action. No precedent existed to support a special relationship because it would impose liability for discretionary governmental acts or omissions granted unqualified immunity by the California Tort Claims Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 810 et seq. Respondents did not breach the mandatory duties imposed by Cal. Penal Code §§ 1203.10 and 1203.12 because the proximate cause element required to establish damages for a public entity's failure to discharge a mandatory duty was not satisfied. Respondents' decision not to revoke probation was also subject to statutory immunity because it was discretionary. Accordingly, the judgment of dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of dismissal was affirmed because the discretionary decision of respondent probation department not to revoke the probation of the defendant who attacked appellant assault victims was subject to statutory immunity. A special relationship based on assistance appellants gave to respondent in a theft investigation would impose liability for impose liability for governmental acts that were granted unqualified immunity.

 

1986 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Water Dist. v. Fair Political Practices Com.


Civ. No. 50917


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


73 Cal. App. 3d 650; 141 Cal. Rptr. 8; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1879



September 23, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 187785, Charles H. Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying a preliminary injunction is affirmed. The writ of supersedeas granted by this court pending appeal is dissolved on the date this opinion becomes final.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, Metropolitan Water District of Southern California and Board Members, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied plaintiffs' complaint to enjoin defendant, Fair Political Practices Commission from compelling plaintiffs' officers and employees to make certain financial disclosures under its conflict of interest code.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, Metropolitan Water District and Board Members, formulated a conflict of interest code pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 87300. The code was submitted to defendant, Fair Political Practices Commission, for approval. Defendant revised portions of the code to prohibit plaintiffs from seeking review of any questionable financial disclosures by its general counsel on a case-by-case and interest-by-interest basis. Plaintiff sought declaratory and injunctive relief against enforcement of the revised code. The trial court denied plaintiffs' complaint. Plaintiff claimed on appeal that it was entitled to some form of individualized review for designated employees before they were required to divulge certain assets because Cal. Gov't Code § 87302(b) allowed it to establish a procedure under which a designated employee could demonstrate that it was not reasonably foreseeable that a decision would have a material financial effect. The court rejected plaintiffs' claims because Section 87302(b) did not provide for a case-by-case evaluation of financial interests. Accordingly, the court affirmed the order denying plaintiff's complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court which denied declaratory and injunctive relief to plaintiffs, Metropolitan Water District of Southern California against defendant, Fair Political Practices Commission. The court ruled that the Fair Political Practices Act did not permit a case-by-case review of individual conflicts of interest.

1988 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Westfield-Palos Verdes Co. v. City of Rancho Palos Verdes


Civ. No. 49838


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


73 Cal. App. 3d 486; 141 Cal. Rptr. 36; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1865



September 20, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified September 30, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 88523, Campbell M. Lucas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land developers sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondent city and dismissed appellants' action seeking to avoid payment of city municipal taxes affecting their housing projects and to obtain refunds of taxes already paid.


OVERVIEW: Appellant land developers challenged a grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent city and dismissal of their action seeking to avoid payment of city municipal taxes affecting their housing projects. Appellants contended that the ordinances were unconstitutionally retroactive, that the taxes were discriminatory, and that the taxes exceeded the city's authority. The court found that the business license tax was a tax upon residential developers, which was measured by the number of dwelling units in construction or completed during the tax year. The tax upon appellants was not retroactive insofar as it was applied to some units which were substantially completed at the time of its enactment. Appellants' business was ongoing and the privilege of engaging in business as to those units substantially completed could validly be assessed in the form of a license tax. The court held that the city taxes challenged constituted a valid business license tax upon the ongoing business of residential construction and was prospective rather than retrospective in application, and that the ordinances declared their purpose as strictly that of raising revenue. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellant land developers and in favor of respondent city in appellants' action seeking to avoid payment of municipal taxes affecting their housing projects. The court held that the city taxes constituted a valid business license tax upon the ongoing business of residential construction, which was prospective rather than retrospective in application, and that their purpose was strictly to raise revenue.

Board of Medical Examiners v. Terminal-Hudson Electronics, Inc.


Civ. No. 49970


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


73 Cal. App. 3d 376; 140 Cal. Rptr. 757; 1977 Cal. App. LEXIS 1852



September 15, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 98058, Charles H. Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the case is remanded to the trial court with instructions to undertake further proceedings consistent with the principles set forth in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant optical firm sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found appellant to be in contempt and permanently enjoined it from advertising, in an action filed by respondents, the Board of Medical Examiners, Board of Optometry (boards), and an optical association, pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 2556, 3129 and 651.3.


OVERVIEW: In an action brought by respondents, the Board of Medical Examiners, Board of Optometry (boards), and an optical association, appellant optical firm was found in contempt and permanently enjoined from advertising the price of eyeglasses or the cost of optical commodities or services pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 2556, 3129 and 651.3.
